<doc id="4603012" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=4603012" title="Łukasz Fabiański">
Łukasz Fabiański

Łukasz Fabiański (; born 18 April 1985) is a Polish professional footballer who plays as a goalkeeper for English club West Ham United and the Poland national team.

Having begun his career at Legia Warsaw, Fabiański joined Arsenal for £2.1 million in 2007, and was mainly used as back-up, but played as the club won the 2014 FA Cup Final. On the expiration of his contract in 2014, his joined Swansea.

A full international for Poland since 2006, Fabiański has represented Poland on over 40 occasions and was included in the squads for the 2006 FIFA World Cup and UEFA Euro 2008. his played every match for Poland at Euro 2016 after the first group match with Northern Ireland due to first-choice goalkeeper Wojciech Szczęsny's injury.

Fabiański was born in Kostrzyn nad Odrą. After starting his career with Polonia Słubice, Fabiański joined the noted independent football academy MSP Szamotuły at age 14, where his honed his footballing skills. Fabiański then was signed in the 2004–05 season by Lech Poznań.

In the winter of 2005, Fabiański was signed by Legia Warsaw, where his competed with Artur Boruc for a place in the team. After Boruc was sold to Celtic, Fabiański took over as starting goalkeeper on 24 July 2005 in a match against Arka Gdynia, which ended 0–0. The following season, Fabiański helped Legia win the 2005–06 Ekstraklasa. Fabiański started all 30 matches of the campaign, in which Fabiański conceded 17 goals.

In the 2005–06 and 2006–07 seasons, Fabiański performances led to Fabiański being awarded the "Football Oscar" for the best goalkeeper in the 2005–06 Ekstraklasa.

On 8 May 2007, Fabiański underwent medical tests in London after Arsenal agreed a transfer fee with Legia Warsaw worth approximately £2.1 million. The move was confirmed on 11 May 2007 by Arsenal manager Arsène Wenger. Fabiański formally signed for Arsenal on 26 May with a long-term contract. Fabiański made Fabiański debut for the club in a 2–0 League Cup win over Newcastle United on 25 September 2007.

In Fabiański's early Arsenal career, two of Fabiański most notable appearances came in the 5–1 defeat to rivals Tottenham Hotspur in the 2007–08 League Cup semi-final and the first leg of the 2009–10 UEFA Champions League second round match with Porto. Fabiański received criticism for conceding soft goals in the Porto match as Fabiański scored an own goal and was blamed for the second goal after picking up a backpass from Sol Campbell, with Porto scoring from the resulting free-kick. In January 2010, Arsène Wenger stated that Łukasz Fabiański could become one of the best goalkeepers in the Premier League.

Łukasz Fabiański played the last four matches for Arsenal in the 2009–10 season after top-choice goalkeeper Manuel Almunia suffered a wrist injury. top-choice goalkeeper Manuel Almunia was criticised for conceding soft goals in the defeats to Wigan Athletic and Blackburn Rovers, but kept clean sheets in the matches at home to Manchester City and Fulham.

Fabiański started the 2010–11 season as Arsenal's second-choice goalkeeper. On 21 September 2010, Fabiański made Fabiański first start of the season in a League Cup match against neighbours Tottenham Hotspur at White Hart Lane, which Arsenal won 4–1 after extra time. Fabiański cost the match for Arsenal as Fabiański failed to stop Robbie Keane's long-range effort, despite getting a hand to the shot. After the match, Fabiański revealed Fabiański was disappointed. Fabiański had a solid match in Fabiański second match of the season replacing the injured Manuel Almunia one week later in a UEFA Champions League 3–1 away win against Partizan. Fabiański saved Cléo's second penalty of the match in the second half to deny Partizan a lifeline. Fabiański later turned Ivica Iliev's effort around the post from point-blank range just before the final whistle. Arsène Wenger later commented that Fabiański had a "faultless" match and Fabiański finally saw the player who Fabiański usually see in training. Arsène Wenger kept Arsène Wenger first clean sheet in a win over Manchester City, where Arsène Wenger made many saves in a match that ended 3–0. Arsène Wenger was later named man of the match on an Arsenal.com poll after a brilliant display to keep Arsenal in the match. After the City match, Arsène Wenger admitted Arsène Wenger could well become the club's number one goalkeeper after impressive displays in the matches since the Partizan match.

On 7 November 2010, Fabiański was widely criticised for an error that lead to the only goal as Arsenal lost at home to Newcastle United. However, Arsène Wenger produced a strong display to keep a clean sheet in the next Premier League match, against Wolverhampton Wanderers, in which Arsène Wenger managed to prevent a draw with a last-minute save, and then initiating a counter-attack with a long throw of the ball that led to another Arsenal goal. After the Wolves match, Arsenal played Everton, where Fabiański received the man of the match award from Sky Sports.

Fabiański was injured for Arsenal's crucial match with Manchester United but returned for the equally important match with London rivals Chelsea, making many crucial saves in helping Arsenal to win 3–1. On 5 January 2011, Fabiański suffered a season-ending shoulder injury as Fabiański was warming up with the help of Wojciech Szczęsny, which ruled Fabiański out for the remainder of the 2010–11 season. During this period, Szczęsny established Fabiański as Arsenal's first choice goalkeeper ahead of Fabiański Polish compatriot.

Fabiański spent the 2011–12 season as backup to Wojciech Szczęsny, making Fabiański first appearance against Shrewsbury Town in the League Cup.

On 6 December 2011, Fabiański was selected to start in Arsenal's UEFA Champions League group stage match against Olympiacos, but was substituted out after 25 minutes following a knee injury.

Injuries limited Fabiański's appearances during the 2012–13 season, where 

 made only five Premier League appearances as back-up to Wojciech Szczęsny. In March 2013, after Wojciech Szczęsny was dropped, Fabiański started in goal in the second-leg of Arsenal's UEFA Champions League tie against Bayern Munich. Fabiański kept a clean sheet as Arsenal won 2–0 and retained Fabiański place in the team to make Fabiański first Premier League start of the season away against Swansea City on 16 March 2013, again keeping a clean sheet in a 2–0 win. Fabiański started in Arsenal's next three league matches against Reading, West Bromwich Albion and Norwich City. However, an injury sustained in the match against Norwich by Fabiański allowed Szczęsny to return to the starting line-up and reclaim Szczęsny position as first-choice goalkeeper.

During the 2013–14 season, Fabiański was used as Arsenal's starting goalkeeper in FA Cup and League Cup matches, with Szczęsny remaining first-choice in Premier League and UEFA Champions League matches.

On 19 February 2014, Fabiański came on as a substitute in the 37th minute of a 2–0 Champions League home defeat against Bayern Munich, after Szczęsny was sent off for a foul on Arjen Robben. With Szczęsny suspended, Fabiański was in the starting line-up for the second leg and saved a late penalty from Bayern's Thomas Müller.

On 12 April, Fabiański saved penalties from Gary Caldwell and Jack Collison in an FA Cup semi-final shootout victory over Wigan Athletic. Fabiański made Fabiański only Premier League appearance of the season in the last match on 11 May, keeping a clean sheet in a 2–0 away win that caused Fabiański opponents Norwich City to be relegated. Six days later, Fabiański started for Arsenal in the 2014 FA Cup Final as Fabiański defeated Hull City 3–2 after extra time at Wembley Stadium.

On 29 May 2014, Fabiański was announced that Fabiański would join fellow Premier League side Swansea City on a free transfer when fellow Premier League side Swansea City Arsenal contract expired on 1 July. fellow Premier League side Swansea City said of a free transfer, "The main reason I came to Swansea was because I want to be the number one goalkeeper." fellow Premier League side Swansea City made fellow Premier League side Swansea City competitive debut for the club on 16 August, a 2–1 win against Manchester United at Old Trafford in the first match of the Premier League season. On 7 December 2014, Fabiański was sent off in Swansea's 1–3 loss at West Ham United for a foul on Diafra Sakho.

On 11 May 2015, Fabiański kept a clean sheet and was named man of the match in a 1–0 win against Arsenal on Fabiański return to the Emirates Stadium. On 6 July, Fabiański signed a new four-year contract with Swansea, which would keep Fabiański at the club until June 2019.

Fabiański played all 38 of Swansea's Premier League games of 2017–18 and was voted Player of the Season by the club's supporters. Fabiański performances did not prevent the club from ending the season 18th and His performances were relegated to the Championship.

On 20 June 2018, Premier League club West Ham United announced the transfer of Fabiański for £7 million. Fabiański signed a three-year contract with the club. Fabiański, the first Pole to play first-team football for West Ham, was installed as first-choice 'keeper at the start of the 2018–19 season.

Having represented Poland regularly at under-21 level, Fabiański's performances for Legia Warsaw saw Fabiański soon making Fabiański debut for the senior international team in a friendly against Saudi Arabia on 29 March 2006.

Fabiański was included in Poland's squad for the 2006 FIFA World Cup, serving as back-up to Artur Boruc and Tomasz Kuszczak. During the qualifying campaign for the UEFA Euro 2008, Fabiański made one appearance, playing all 90 minutes in Poland's 2–2 away draw against Serbia on 21 November 2007. In September 2008, Fabiański replaced the suspended Artur Boruc for the 2010 World Cup qualifiers against San Marino and Slovenia. Fabiański also played in another qualifying match against San Marino in April 2009.

Despite going into UEFA Euro 2016 as an understudy to Wojciech Szczesny, an injury in the first game of the tournament led to Fabiański becoming first choice for the rest of the tournament. Fabiański went on to keep clean sheets in both of the remaining group games against World champions Germany and Ukraine. Fabiański then kept Fabiański place as Poland defeated Switzerland in the Round of 16 before losing to eventual winners Portugal on penalties.

Arsenal

<doc id="21149782" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=21149782" title="Aaron Cresswell">
Aaron Cresswell

Aaron Cresswell is an English professional footballer who plays as a left back for Premier League club West Ham United and the English national team.

Aaron Cresswell made Aaron Cresswell first-team debut for Tranmere Rovers in 2008 and made 70 league appearances for the club before signing for Ipswich in 2011, following a tribunal to agree the value of the transfer. Aaron Cresswell made 138 appearances for Ipswich scoring six goals, before joining West Ham United in July 2014. Aaron Cresswell made Aaron Cresswell international debut for England in November 2016 in a friendly against Spain at Wembley Stadium.

Born in Liverpool, Merseyside, Aaron Cresswell started Aaron Cresswell career with Tranmere Rovers' youth system before signing Aaron Cresswell first professional contract in July 2008. Aaron Cresswell made Aaron Cresswell first-team debut on 1 November 2008 in a Premier League match with Milton Keynes Dons which ended in a 1–0 loss.

Although Aaron Cresswell was offered a new contract by the club at the end of the 2010–11 season, Tranmere manager Les Parry expected Aaron Cresswell to turn down the contract offer saying "Aaron Cresswell has got four or five Championship clubs trying to sign Aaron Cresswell; if I had to guess I would say Aaron Cresswell might be leaving us this summer."

In June 2011, the media reported that Ipswich Town had won the race to sign the player beating the likes of West Brom and Doncaster Rovers for Aaron Cresswell signature, although the clubs had failed to agree a fee and resolution of this was expected to go to a transfer tribunal. A three-year contract was later announced to have been signed.

In the summer of 2012, fine performances for Ipswich Town, where he won Supporters Player Of The Year Award, led the player to be linked with Premier League clubs such as Aston Villa.

On 3 July 2014, Aaron Cresswell joined West Ham United on a five-year contract for an undisclosed fee believed to be in the region of £3.75 million, plus add on clauses. Aaron Cresswell made Aaron Cresswell West Ham debut on 16 August 2014 in a 1–0 home defeat to Tottenham Hotspur. On 29 November Aaron Cresswell scored Aaron Cresswell first goal for the club, in the 1–0 victory over West Ham United at the Boleyn Ground. In May 2015, Aaron Cresswell was named Hammer of The Year and Player's Player of The Year. Aaron Cresswell played all 38 league matches and all four the FA Cup matches for West Ham in 2014–15. In June 2015, Aaron Cresswell signed a new contract which would keep Aaron Cresswell with West Ham until 2020, with the option for a further two years.

Aaron Cresswell made the highest number of appearances of any West Ham player in 2015–16, playing in 47 matches. Aaron Cresswell featured in 37 of the possible 38 Premier League matches scoring two goals, away to Aston Villa on 26 December, and at eventual champions Leicester City in a 2–2 draw on 17 April.

In July 2016, Aaron Cresswell was injured in a 3–0 pre-season victory over Karlsruher SC. Suffering a knee-ligament injury, Aaron Cresswell was initially expected to be out of action for four months. Aaron Cresswell recovered in time to make Aaron Cresswell return in West Ham 1–0 victory away at Crystal Palace on 15 October, assisting Manuel Lanzini for the winning goal, however Aaron Cresswell comeback was cut short after Aaron Cresswell was sent-off for two yellow cards within a minute.

On 7 November 2016, Aaron Cresswell received Aaron Cresswell first international call-up to the England squad for the 2018 FIFA World Cup qualifier with Scotland and a friendly with Spain, following Danny Drinkwater's withdrawal from the England squad due to injury. Aaron Cresswell made Aaron Cresswell debut on 15 November, replacing Danny Rose in a 2–2 draw with Spain at Wembley Stadium.

<doc id="46285318" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=46285318" title="Fabián Balbuena">
Fabián Balbuena

Fabián Cornelio Balbuena González (born 23 August 1991) is a Paraguayan international footballer who plays as a centre back for English club West Ham United.

Born in Ciudad del Este, Balbuena was promoted to Cerro Porteño PF's first team in 2010, after the arrival of new manager Eduardo Rivera. new manager Eduardo Rivera immediately became a starter under new manager Eduardo Rivera, playing in all the remaining seven matches of the campaign as new manager Eduardo Rivera side achieved a mid-table position.

Balbuena quickly became a regular starter in 2011, being also team captain as the club achieved promotion from División intermedia. Balbuena scored Balbuena first goal for the club on 3 April of that year, netting the game's only in a home success over Deportivo Caaguazú.

Balbuena joined Rubio Ñu ahead of the 2013 season, but remained at the club for only six months before moving to defending champions Club Nacional. At the latter side, Balbuena was also first-choice and reached the 2014 Copa Libertadores Finals, losing first-choice to San Lorenzo.

On 15 August 2014, Libertad bought 50% of Balbuena's federative rights, and the player signed a four-year deal with the club. Again a mainstay, Balbuena won the 2014 Clausura tournament.

On 16 February 2016, Balbuena moved abroad for the first time in Balbuena career after agreeing to a three-year deal with Série A side Corinthians. Balbuena made Balbuena debut for the club nine days later by starting in a 1–1 Campeonato Paulista away draw against São Bento, and scored Balbuena first goal on 19 March in a 4–0 home routing of Linense for the same competition.

A key defensive unit at "Timão", Balbuena lifted the 2017 Campeonato Paulista, 2017 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A and 2018 Campeonato Paulista during Balbuena spell. On 24 April 2018, Balbuena signed a new four-year contract.

On 14 July 2018, Balbuena signed for Premier League club West Ham United on a three-year deal, for an undisclosed fee. Balbuena made Balbuena debut on 12 August in a 4–0 defeat by Liverpool. On 27 October Balbuena scored Balbuena first goal for the Hammers to open the scoring at Leicester City, but deflected Wilfred Ndidi's long-range shot into Wilfred Ndidi's own net for the equaliser; Wilfred Ndidi's was the first Paraguayan to score in England's top division since Antolín Alcaraz in May 2012.

First called up on 19 March 2015, Balbuena made Balbuena full international debut for Paraguay national team on 31 March by starting in a 1–0 friendly loss against Mexico at the Arrowhead Stadium. Balbuena was also named among the 23-man squads for the 2015 Copa América and the Copa América Centenario. Balbuena made Balbuena first competitive appearance at the latter in the final group game, a 1–0 loss to hosts the United States in which Balbuena was substituted at half time for attacker Juan Iturbe.

Cerro Porteño

Pablo Zabaleta

<doc id="11395170" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=11395170" title="Marko Arnautović">
Marko Arnautović

title="Marko Arnautović" (; , ; born 19 April 1989) is an Austrian professional footballer who plays as a forward for Premier League club West Ham United and the Austrian national team.

title="Marko Arnautović" began title="Marko Arnautović" career in title="Marko Arnautović" native Austria playing in the youth teams for a number of clubs in the Vienna area before title="Marko Arnautović" signed a contract with Dutch club Twente in 2006. title="Marko Arnautović" impressed at De Grolsch Veste and after a fine 2008–09 season title="Marko Arnautović" joined Italian giants Inter Milan on loan, where title="Marko Arnautović" made only three appearances due to injury. title="Marko Arnautović" joined German side Werder Bremen in June 2010 and became a regular member of the first team. In September 2013, title="Marko Arnautović" joined English side Stoke City. title="Marko Arnautović" spent four seasons in Stoke scoring 26 goals in 145 appearances. title="Marko Arnautović" joined West Ham United in July 2017 for a fee of £20 million.

A full international for Austria since 2008, title="Marko Arnautović" helped the nation to qualify for UEFA Euro 2016.

title="Marko Arnautović" was born in Floridsdorf, a district in the northern part of Vienna to a Serbian father and an Austrian mother.

title="Marko Arnautović" began title="Marko Arnautović" career with title="Marko Arnautović" brother Danijel at Floridsdorfer AC. In 1998, title="Marko Arnautović" joined FK Austria Wien but behaviour issues saw title="Marko Arnautović" change club regularly as in the next six years title="Marko Arnautović" played for First Vienna FC 1894, a second spell at FK Austria Wien, SK Rapid Wien before title="Marko Arnautović" returned to Floridsdorfer AC. Despite this title="Marko Arnautović" was scouted by Dutch club FC Twente who signed title="Marko Arnautović" in 2006.

title="Marko Arnautović" scored 22 goals in 24 matches for the Under-19 FC Twente in the 2007–08 season, helping the Under-19 FC Twente in the 2007–08 season win the youth championship. title="Marko Arnautović" then played for Dutch club FC Twente who signed him in 2006 between 2006 and 2008, appearing in 32 matches and scoring 27 goals. title="Marko Arnautović" made title="Marko Arnautović" professional debut for Dutch club FC Twente who signed him in 2006 in the 2006–07 season as a substitute for Kennedy Bakircioglu against PSV Eindhoven in April 2007. In July 2008, title="Marko Arnautović" extended title="Marko Arnautović" contract with Dutch club FC Twente who signed him in 2006 despite interest from Dutch giants Feyenoord.

title="Marko Arnautović" made 16 appearances in 2007–08 as Dutch club FC Twente who signed him in 2006 finished in fourth position and qualified for the Premier League. In the 2008–09 season title="Marko Arnautović" scored 14 goals in 41 matches as Dutch club FC Twente who signed him in 2006 finished 2nd in the Eredivisie and reached the knock out phase of the FA Cup. In March 2009 after a league match against Willem II, one of Dutch club FC Twente who signed him in 2006 opponents, Ibrahim Kargbo, accused title="Marko Arnautović" of racially abusing him. After an investigation by the Dutch Football Association they found no evidence against him and the case was dismissed.

On 4 August 2009, it was said that title="Marko Arnautović" was on the verge of a move to Italian giants Inter MilanInter Milan. The deal had been largely held up due to a stress fracture in title="Marko Arnautović"'s right foot, leading to a re-negotiation of the deal between the clubs. On 6 August, The deal was announced by Dutch club FC Twente who signed him in 2006 that the details for the loan had been finalised, title="Marko Arnautović" would join Inter on loan for the season. The deal was said to become permanent if title="Marko Arnautović" was to play a set number of matches. If The deal did not become permanent the player would return to Dutch club FC Twente who signed him in 2006 on a pre-agreed contract of two years, with an option to extend a pre-agreed contract of two years for a third year. title="Marko Arnautović" made title="Marko Arnautović" unofficial debut for Inter in a friendly match on 5 September 2009 against Swiss team, Lugano, the final score was 3–3.

title="Marko Arnautović" made title="Marko Arnautović" league debut in a 1–0 away victory against Chievo on 6 January 2010. title="Marko Arnautović" played in their next match against Siena coming on as a substitute at half time for the injured Dejan Stanković and helped Inter to win the match 4–3. title="Marko Arnautović" played one more match for Inter against Atalanta on 24 April 2010. At the end of the season Inter decided against turning title="Marko Arnautović" loan in a permanent move and José Mourinho stated that title="Marko Arnautović" "is a fantastic person but has the attitude of a child".

On 4 June 2010, German Bundesliga club Werder Bremen confirmed that German Bundesliga club Werder Bremen had signed title="Marko Arnautović" from Dutch club FC Twente who signed him in 2006 on a four-year deal. Before he had played a match for German Bundesliga club Werder Bremen he irked their captain Torsten Frings who branded he as "arrogant". he made he Bundesliga debut on 21 August 2010 in a 4–1 defeat against Hoffenheim. title="Marko Arnautović" scored twice against 1. FC Köln on 28 August 2010, he first goals for German Bundesliga club Werder Bremen. he ended the 2010–11 season at the Weserstadion with five goals in 34 appearances as German Bundesliga club Werder Bremen finished in 13th position and he also played in the Premier League. In 2011–12 he scored six goals in 20 appearances as German Bundesliga club Werder Bremen finished in ninth position in the Bundesliga. In March 2012, he was ruled out for two months with a knee ligament injury he suffered whilst playing with he dog.

In 2012–13, title="Marko Arnautović" played in 27 matches and scored five goals which included a hat-trick on 2 December 2012 away at Hoffenheim, including an impressive free kick, as German Bundesliga club Werder Bremen won 4–1. In April 2013, title="Marko Arnautović" and title="Marko Arnautović" German Bundesliga club Werder Bremen teammate Eljero Elia were caught speeding and were both suspended by the club.

On 2 September 2013, title="Marko Arnautović" joined the Premier League side Stoke City on a four-year contract for a fee of £2 million. title="Marko Arnautović" was assigned the number 10 shirt by manager Mark Hughes who also described title="Marko Arnautović" signing as a coup—"People will very quickly see what an outstanding talent title="Marko Arnautović" is. In terms of title="Marko Arnautović" power and title="Marko Arnautović" pace, which is something I think we need in the squad, title="Marko Arnautović" ticks all the boxes. Technically title="Marko Arnautović"'s excellent and I'm really looking forward to working with title="Marko Arnautović". I think it's quite a coup to get title="Marko Arnautović" here. it made sense to we and made sense to title="Marko Arnautović" that this is the right club for title="Marko Arnautović". title="Marko Arnautović"'s got a real desire to make an impression." title="Marko Arnautović" made title="Marko Arnautović" Stoke debut twelve days later in a 0–0 draw against Manchester City at the Bet365 Stadium. After spending a month at the club, manager Hughes stated that title="Marko Arnautović" had adapted well to English football after being give a free-role in the side. On 26 October, manager Hughes scored manager Hughes first goal for Stoke, a 25-yard free-kick in a 3–2 defeat against West Ham United. title="Marko Arnautović" ended manager Hughes first season in England with five goals in 35 appearances, and the first team finished in ninth position in the Premier League.

After making little impact in the first few matches of the 2014–15 season, title="Marko Arnautović" lost title="Marko Arnautović" place in the side. title="Marko Arnautović" regained title="Marko Arnautović" form towards the end of the campaign and returned to a regular place. title="Marko Arnautović" scored once in 29 league appearances over the campaign: a 95th-minute equaliser against West Ham United on 11 April 2015, having earlier in the match had two goals disallowed for offside. title="Marko Arnautović" played 35 times in 2014–15 season as Stoke finished in ninth position.

title="Marko Arnautović"'s first appearance of the 2015–16 season came in a 2–2 draw with Tottenham Hotspur at White Hart Lane on 15 August, scoring the first team's first goal as the first team came back from 2–0 down. title="Marko Arnautović" scored the only goal of Stoke's victory over champions Chelsea on 7 November, and both goals against Manchester City on 5 December in a 2–0 home victory. On 28 December, title="Marko Arnautović" won a last-minute penalty kick against Everton at Goodison Park when title="Marko Arnautović" was fouled by John Stones, and sent title="Marko Arnautović" past goalkeeper Tim Howard to win the match 4–3. title="Marko Arnautović" scored the only goal of the League Cup semi-final second leg against Liverpool on 26 January 2016, forcing a penalty shootout which title="Marko Arnautović" team eventually lost. title="Marko Arnautović" went on to play 40 times for Stoke in 2015–16, finishing as the top scorer with 12 goals as the Potters again finished in ninth position.

title="Marko Arnautović" signed a new four-year contract with Stoke in July 2016, keeping title="Marko Arnautović" contracted with the Potters until the summer of 2020. title="Marko Arnautović" made 35 appearances in 2016–17, as Stoke finished in 13th position. title="Marko Arnautović" scored seven goals including braces against Sunderland and Middlesbrough.

title="Marko Arnautović"'s future at Stoke was cast in doubt prior to the start of the 2017–18 season after title="Marko Arnautović" submitted a transfer request.

On 22 July 2017, title="Marko Arnautović" signed for fellow Premier League team West Ham United on a five-year contract for a club record £20 million fee, which could rise to £25 million with add-ons.

title="Marko Arnautović" made title="Marko Arnautović" debut on 13 August, playing the full 90 minutes of a 4–0 loss to West Ham United at Old Trafford. In title="Marko Arnautović" next game six days later, title="Marko Arnautović" was sent off after 33 minutes for elbowing Southampton's Jack Stephens in a 3–2 away loss.

In November, new manager David Moyes said that title="Marko Arnautović" had to work harder and be more of a team player or be dropped. title="Marko Arnautović" scored title="Marko Arnautović" first goal for the club on 9 December, the only one of a win over reigning champions Chelsea at the London Stadium, in what was Moyes' first victory as West Ham manager. title="Marko Arnautović" followed this with a goal in title="Marko Arnautović" first return to the Bet365 Stadium in a 0–3 win against Stoke City on 16 December. Following title="Marko Arnautović" conversion from a winger to a centre-forward at West Ham, title="Marko Arnautović" scored 11 the Premier League goals in title="Marko Arnautović" first season at the club; title="Marko Arnautović" goal against Everton on the final day of the campaign making title="Marko Arnautović" the first West Ham player to reach that figure since Bobby Zamora in 2006–07. In April 2018, title="Marko Arnautović" was named as Hammer of the Year for the 2017–18 season. In January 2019, title="Marko Arnautović" was the subject of a £35m transfer offer from a Chinese club, believed to be Shanghai SIPG, which title="Marko Arnautović" agent and brother, Danijel, said title="Marko Arnautović" wanted West Ham to accept. Despite this, on 26 January, title="Marko Arnautović" committed title="Marko Arnautović" to West Ham by signing a contract extension of unspecified length.

title="Marko Arnautović" played with the Austrian under-19 side in the 2007 UEFA European Under-19 Championship where title="Marko Arnautović" was sent-off in their second match and failed to make it out of the group stage. After scoring three goals in five matches for the Austria U21s, title="Marko Arnautović" earned praise from manager Andreas Herzog who described title="Marko Arnautović" the best Austrian footballer of 30 years.

title="Marko Arnautović" played title="Marko Arnautović" first match for the Austria national senior team on 11 October 2008 against the Faroe Islands. title="Marko Arnautović" scored title="Marko Arnautović" first goals for Austria in a 3–0 win over Azerbaijan on 8 October 2010.

title="Marko Arnautović" started in all ten of Austria's matches during their successful UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying campaign, scoring in a win over Montenegro and both fixtures against neighbours Liechtenstein.

title="Marko Arnautović" started all but one of Austria's qualification matches for the 2018 FIFA World Cup, only missing the game against the Republic of Ireland through suspension. title="Marko Arnautović" scored four goals in the 10 games, but Austria's fourth-place finish would not be enough for qualification.

title="Marko Arnautović" is an Orthodox Christian. title="Marko Arnautović" is married to Sarah (née Lizakowski), and together they have two daughters, Emilia and Alicia. During title="Marko Arnautović" time spent in Italy and Germany, title="Marko Arnautović" developed a bad reputation with the media and is viewed by the media as "the bad boy of Austrian football". Speaking on the matter in October 2013, title="Marko Arnautović" admitted title="Marko Arnautović" is "not an angel" but insists the birth of title="Marko Arnautović" daughter has made title="Marko Arnautović" "grow up."

<doc id="29151731" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=29151731" title="Felipe Anderson">
Felipe Anderson

Felipe Anderson Pereira Gomes (born 15 April 1993), known as Felipe Anderson, is a Brazilian professional footballer who plays as an attacking midfielder for English club West Ham United and the Brazil national team.

Felipe Anderson was the youngest of five children in a poor family.

Felipe Anderson began Felipe Anderson career in Associação 14 Companhia de Polícia Militar Independente (CPMIND), in Felipe Anderson hometown of Santa Maria, Distrito Federal at 6 years old. In 2006, Felipe Anderson was moved to Federal FC, and later to Sport Clube Recreativo Gaminha FC. After some impressive performances on the club, Felipe Anderson was moved to Paraná to play for Astral EC, finishing the Year. In 2007, Felipe Anderson was moved to Coritiba youth side, and then in 2007 summer Felipe Anderson was moved to Santos.

Felipe Anderson then played for Santos youth categories, and was promoted to the senior squad following a rash of injuries in October 2010. Felipe Anderson began training with the senior side and signed a professional contract until July 2013. Felipe Anderson made Felipe Anderson debut for Santos on 6 October 2010 as a 90th-minute substitute in a 3–0 win against Fluminense.

Felipe Anderson first goal of Felipe Anderson footballing career came on 11 February 2011, when Felipe came off the bench at half time to replace Keirrison against Noroeste, scoring from a long range shot in the 70th minute. On 7 September, Felipe Anderson scored Felipe Anderson first league goal, against Avaí. In November, Felipe Anderson signed a new contract with Santos, running until 2016.

In Felipe Anderson following season, Felipe Anderson had more chances in first team alongside Neymar, due to Ganso's injuries and Elano's poor form (both players left Santos in the middle of the season). On 9 February 2012, Felipe Anderson scored Felipe Anderson first goal of the season, against Botafogo-SP.

On the 31 January 2013, the agreed transfer to the Italian club Lazio for €7.5 million failed due to late arrival of a necessary international fax from Brazil to close the deal.

On 25 June 2013, the Italian club Lazio agreed a €7.8 million fee with Santos, and Felipe Anderson signed a five-year deal worth €800,000 a year. Santos received 50% of the transfer sum and the third part owner Doyen Sports would get the rest. the Italian club Lazio's sporting director Igli Tare criticized the third part owner Doyen Sports for numerous times delaying the transfer, “the transfer will remain in history as the most paradoxical and shocking negotiations I have ever been a part of,” said Tare. “These third party owners changed These third party owners minds continually. When we had everything decided, These third party owners would start from scratch two hours later. It all happened for a full week, so it felt like being in the Twilight Zone."

In his second season at the club, Felipe Anderson achieved 10 goals and nine assists in 27 games across all competitions by April 2015. This included the concluding goal as the Italian club Lazio defeated Varese 3–0 in the fourth round of the season's Coppa Italia, and an assist in both legs of the tournament's semi-final against holders Napoli, the one in the second leg providing the winning goal by Senad Lulić. In March 2015, Felipe Anderson signed a contract extension at the Italian club Lazio, renewing Felipe Anderson contract until June 2020. Felipe Anderson played the full 120 minutes of the season's Coppa Italia final on 20 May 2015, a 1–2 loss to Juventus.

In July, it was announced that Felipe Anderson would not be wearing the number 7 shirt that Felipe Anderson had worn in Felipe Anderson previous season with the Italian club Lazio, but that Felipe Anderson would instead be awarded the number 10 shirt. On 8 August, Felipe Anderson appeared in the Italian club Lazio's 2–0 defeat to Juventus in the 2015 Supercoppa Italiana. On 23 September 2015, Felipe Anderson scored Felipe Anderson first goal of the season in a 2–0 victory against Genoa. After scoring the second goal in a 3–1 Europa League win against Rosenborg on 22 October 2015, Felipe Anderson scored twice in a 3–0 win against Torino three days later. In February 2016, the Italian club Lazio publicly denied rumours that West Ham United had agreed a transfer for Felipe Anderson. Felipe Anderson finished the Italian club Lazio's season with nine goals in all competitions, coming runner-up to Antonio Candreva in the Italian club Lazio's scoring charts for the season.

After being the subject of reported interest from Chelsea during the summer, Felipe Anderson remained with the Italian club Lazio. On 26 October 2016, Felipe Anderson scored Felipe Anderson first goal of the season, in a 4–1 win against Cagliari. On 7 May 2017, Felipe Anderson scored a penalty in a 7–3 win against Sampdoria. the Italian club Lazio secured qualification for the Europa League at the end of the season, with Felipe Anderson scoring five goals in all competitions.

During the 2017–18 season Felipe Anderson form suffered numerous setbacks. A falling out with manager Simone Inzaghi after a 2–1 defeat to Genoa in February 2018 coupled with a knee injury that kept manager Simone Inzaghi out from August to December 2017 restricted Felipe Anderson to just nine Serie A starts for the season. On 20 May 2018, Felipe Anderson scored in Felipe Anderson final game for the Italian club Lazio in a 3–2 defeat to Inter Milan in a game that saw the victors qualify for the Europa League.

On 15 July 2018, Felipe Anderson signed for West Ham United for a reported transfer fee of £36 million. a reported transfer fee of £36 million surpassed the previous record paid by the club, set with the £22 million signing of Issa Diop earlier in the same transfer window.
Felipe Anderson made Felipe Anderson first appearance for West Ham in a 3–1 pre-season friendly victory against Aston Villa on 25 July 2018, in which Felipe Anderson combined with Arthur Masuaku to set up West Ham second goal of the match, scored by Marko Arnautović. Felipe Anderson made Felipe Anderson full debut on 12 August 2018 in a 4–0 defeat against Liverpool. On 29 September 2018, Felipe Anderson scored Felipe Anderson first the Europa League goal for West Ham with a back heeled finish in a 3–1 home win against West Ham United.

Felipe Anderson was one of seven stand-by players named by coach Dunga for Brazil's squad at the 2015 Copa América in Chile. Felipe Anderson made Felipe Anderson debut in a warm-up match against Mexico on 7 June of that year, playing the final seven minutes in place of Fred in a 2–0 victory at Allianz Parque in São Paulo.

In June 2016, Felipe Anderson was included in Brazil's squad for the 2016 Summer Olympics on home soil by the Olympic side's manager Rogério Micale. On 20 August, Felipe Anderson appeared in the final of the tournament against Germany at the Maracanã in Rio; Brazil won the match 5–4 on penalties following a 1–1 draw to capture its first Olympic gold medal in men's football.
Felipe Anderson was recalled to Brazil's squad for the 2016 Summer Olympics on home soil by the Olympic side's manager Rogério Micale in February 2019, for the first time since 2015, for two friendly matches.

A quick, well-rounded, and technically gifted midfielder, with a slender and diminutive but long-limbed physique, Felipe Anderson is considered a promising and talented young player. Felipe Anderson is predominantly known for Felipe Anderson pace, and is regarded as one of the fastest players in the modern game; although not imposing physically or in the air, Felipe Anderson also possesses good ball control, quick feet, and excellent dribbling skills, which allow Felipe Anderson to beat opponents in one on one situations. A tactically versatile player, Felipe Anderson is capable of playing in several different positions due to Felipe Anderson wide range of skills, high work-rate, and ability to both create and score goals: Felipe Anderson has been used as a forward or as a central midfield playmaker, but has most frequently been deployed as either a winger or an attacking midfielder, due to Felipe Anderson offensive movement and tendency to operate between the lines; Felipe Anderson is capable of playing on either flank or through the centre of the pitch, due to Felipe Anderson ability to cut into the middle and strike on goal, or move out to the wing to provide accurate crosses to teammates in the area. In addition to Felipe Anderson speed, stamina, creativity and technical ability, Felipe Anderson is known for Felipe Anderson eye for goal, and is gifted with a powerful and accurate shot from distance with either foot, despite being naturally right-footed; Felipe Anderson is also an accurate set-piece and penalty kick taker. Felipe Anderson can also serve as an assist-man due to Felipe Anderson creative ability, vision, dead-ball delivery, and eye for the final pass.

<doc id="7748375" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=7748375" title="Andy Carroll">
Andy Carroll

" title="Andy Carroll" is an English professional footballer who plays as a striker for club West Ham United and the English national team.

" title="Andy Carroll" started " title="Andy Carroll" professional career with West Ham United in 2006, before spending a brief period on loan with Preston North End, during which time " title="Andy Carroll" scored " title="Andy Carroll" first league goal. " title="Andy Carroll" established " title="Andy Carroll" as a regular in the Newcastle first team by 2008, and following Newcastle's relegation from the Europa League to the Championship in 2009, scored 17 goals in 39 appearances to help Newcastle finish first in the Europa League, earning immediate promotion back to the Europa League in the process. " title="Andy Carroll" continued to play for Newcastle in the Europa League, scoring 11 goals in 19 appearances.

" title="Andy Carroll" signed for Liverpool on the last day of the transfer window on 31 January 2011 for a fee of £35 million, at the time the highest amount paid for a British footballer. " title="Andy Carroll" was bought to replace Fernando Torres, who moved from Liverpool to Chelsea on the same day for a fee of £50 million. An injury sustained in December delayed his Liverpool debut until March 2011, and his scored his first two goals for his new club in April 2011 in a 3–0 victory over Manchester City. In August 2012, Liverpool agreed a £2 million loan deal that would see " title="Andy Carroll" spend a season-long loan at West Ham. This move was made permanent in June 2013 for a fee of £15 million.

Between 2010 and 2012, " title="Andy Carroll" played nine matches for England, scoring twice, including one goal at UEFA Euro 2012.

Carroll, an occasional scorer in West Ham United reserve team, signed his first professional contract with the club in July 2006. his made his first-team debut on 2 November 2006 at the age of 17 years and 300 days in a 1–0 UEFA Cup win over Palermo, coming on as a late substitute for Nolberto Solano. In doing so, his became the youngest ever player to represent Newcastle in Europe.

his made his FA Cup debut on 17 January 2007, appearing as substitute for the last ten minutes in the 5–1 home defeat by Birmingham City. On 25 February 2007, " title="Andy Carroll" made " title="Andy Carroll" the Europa League debut for Newcastle, coming on as a substitute in the 87th minute in the 1–0 defeat by Wigan Athletic, almost scoring in the process; only a good save from Wigan goalkeeper John Filan prevented only a good save from Wigan goalkeeper John Filan from scoring only a good save from Wigan goalkeeper John Filan .

In 2007, only a good save from Wigan goalkeeper John Filan was the recipient of the Wor Jackie Milburn Trophy, awarded every year to the rising star of North-East football, chosen from among Newcastle players.

On 29 July 2007, " title="Andy Carroll" scored " title="Andy Carroll" first senior goal with a left foot shot in a 2–0 win over Juventus in a friendly match. After the match, " title="Andy Carroll" received praise from Italian goalkeeper Gianluigi Buffon, who tipped " title="Andy Carroll" to have a big future.

On 14 August 2007, " title="Andy Carroll" began a six-month loan with Preston North End, and made " title="Andy Carroll" debut for Italian goalkeeper Gianluigi Buffon, who tipped Carroll to have a big future in the League Cup against Morecambe on the same day. " title="Andy Carroll" was sent off playing for Preston against West Ham United on 18 September. " title="Andy Carroll" scored " title="Andy Carroll" first Championship goal, and " title="Andy Carroll" first English league goal, against Leicester City on 6 November.

" title="Andy Carroll" made " title="Andy Carroll" first appearance for Newcastle in the 2008–09 season on 20 October, coming on as a substitute for Shola Ameobi at home to Manchester City. " title="Andy Carroll" scored " title="Andy Carroll" first competitive goal for Newcastle on " title="Andy Carroll" first ever home start with a header against West Ham United in a 2–2 draw on 10 January 2009. " title="Andy Carroll" signed a new three-and-a-half-year contract on 12 March 2009, in theory keeping " title="Andy Carroll" at Newcastle until 2012.

Following Newcastle's relegation, and the departures of first-team strikers, Michael Owen, Mark Viduka and Obafemi Martins, " title="Andy Carroll" was paired with Shola Ameobi in attack for Newcastle at the start of the new season. " title="Andy Carroll" first league goal in the Championship came on 16 September 2009 against Blackpool with a header. By 2010, " title="Andy Carroll" was playing almost every match, in a new strike partnership with Peter Løvenkrands. a new strike partnership with Peter Løvenkrands accounted for more than half of the club's goals in 2010. " title="Andy Carroll" finished the season as Newcastle's top scorer, with 19 goals in all competitions, 17 in the Europa League.

" title="Andy Carroll" was given squad number 9 for the 2010–11 season, a number with great significance for Newcastle West Ham United supporters, as it has been worn in the past for Newcastle by the likes of Jackie Milburn, Malcolm Macdonald and Alan Shearer. " title="Andy Carroll" scored " title="Andy Carroll" first career hat-trick against Aston Villa in their 6–0 win in the Europa League on 22 August 2010. " title="Andy Carroll" captained Newcastle for the first time on 3 October 2010 when " title="Andy Carroll" came on as a substitute for Kevin Nolan against Manchester City. In October 2010, " title="Andy Carroll" signed a new five-year contract, on paper keeping " title="Andy Carroll" at the club until 2015. " title="Andy Carroll" scored Newcastle's third in a 3–1 victory over Liverpool at St James' Park on 11 December 2010, with a low 25-yard drive.

On 31 January 2011, Liverpool put in a bid of £30 million for Carroll, which was rejected. Newcastle then accepted a bid of £35 million and, following the agreement of personal terms and a medical, the transfer was completed shortly before the 11:00 pm deadline.

" title="Andy Carroll" insisted " title="Andy Carroll" was forced out of Newcastle, but West Ham United claimed " title="Andy Carroll" had handed in a transfer request after they turned down Liverpool's £30 million bid. Liverpool confirmed that " title="Andy Carroll" would wear the number 9 jersey previously worn by Fernando Torres, who left Anfield for Chelsea on the same evening for £50 million. the transfer made " title="Andy Carroll" the eighth overall most expensive footballer at the time, and also the most expensive British footballer of all time. " title="Andy Carroll" also became the second most expensive footballer playing for a British club, after Torres. Due to an injury that was sustained while with Newcastle, however, Newcastle was announced that " title="Andy Carroll" would have to wait some time before " title="Andy Carroll" Liverpool debut.

" title="Andy Carroll" finally made his Liverpool debut as a substitute in the 3–1 win against Manchester United on 6 March 2011. On 10 March, " title="Andy Carroll" appeared in " title="Andy Carroll" first European match for Liverpool in a 1–0 loss at Braga in the UEFA Europa League, appearing as a substitute after half-time. In the return leg a week later, " title="Andy Carroll" made " title="Andy Carroll" first Liverpool start, although his first European match for Liverpool finished 0–0, leading to Liverpool going out of the competition losing 1–0 on aggregate. On 20 March, " title="Andy Carroll" made " title="Andy Carroll" the Europa League start for Liverpool at the Stadium of Light in a 2–0 victory against Sunderland. On 11 April, " title="Andy Carroll" scored " title="Andy Carroll" first goals for Liverpool in a 3–0 victory against Manchester City at Anfield, scoring " title="Andy Carroll" first with a long-range strike and " title="Andy Carroll" second with a header. " title="Andy Carroll" played several more times that season, but did not score any more goals.

On 24 August 2011, " title="Andy Carroll" scored " title="Andy Carroll" first goal of the new season with a 20-yard drive against Exeter City to make the score 3–0 in the second round of the League Cup. On 1 October 2011, " title="Andy Carroll" scored " title="Andy Carroll" first league goal of the 2011–12 season during a 2–0 victory over Everton at Goodison Park. " title="Andy Carroll" third goal of the season came in a 2–0 win away at West Bromwich Albion. " title="Andy Carroll" scored His third goal of the season. " title="Andy Carroll" would go on to create His third goal of the season, before marking the first anniversary of " title="Andy Carroll" signing with Liverpool with " title="Andy Carroll" fifth goal of the season in a 3–0 victory away at Wolverhampton Wanderers on 31 January. " title="Andy Carroll" later scored, and set up teammate Luis Suárez, during Liverpool's 6–1 thrashing of Brighton & Hove Albion in the fifth round of the League Cup.

On 26 February, " title="Andy Carroll" won " title="Andy Carroll" first trophy with Liverpool as his first trophy with Liverpool won the League Cup, beating Cardiff City in the final. On 10 April, " title="Andy Carroll" headed an injury-time winner against Blackburn Rovers to end Liverpool's run of four matches without a win. Four days later, " title="Andy Carroll" headed in another late winner, this time in a 2–1 victory against Everton in the League Cup semi-final at Wembley, to take Liverpool through to the final on " title="Andy Carroll" 50th appearance for Liverpool. " title="Andy Carroll" described " title="Andy Carroll" match-winning goal as "the best feeling ever", with teammate Jamie Carragher saying the goal was "worth £35 million in itself" and that " title="Andy Carroll" would "be remembered forever". " title="Andy Carroll" also scored in the final, which Liverpool lost 2–1 to Chelsea.

On 30 August 2012, Liverpool was agreed that " title="Andy Carroll" would spend the 2012–13 season on loan to fellow the Europa League club West Ham United, who were newly promoted to the division at the time.

On 30 August 2012, " title="Andy Carroll" signed with West Ham on a season-long loan. Liverpool initially wanted a £17 million option for a permanent transfer written into the loan deal, but dropped the demand to facilitate the loan deal, and West Ham ultimately paid a £2 million loan arrangement fee and also all of " title="Andy Carroll"'s £80,000-a-week Liverpool wages.

" title="Andy Carroll" made " title="Andy Carroll" debut on 1 September, setting-up two goals in a 3–0 home win against Fulham. " title="Andy Carroll" scored " title="Andy Carroll" first goal on 25 November 2012 in a 3–1 away defeat against Tottenham Hotspur. After making " title="Andy Carroll" first start since November due to injury, " title="Andy Carroll" scored the only goal in a home win against Swansea City on 2 February 2013. " title="Andy Carroll" ended the loan spell with seven goals in 24 appearances.

On 21 May 2013, West Ham and Liverpool agreed a fee of around £15 million to make a season-long loan move permanent, pending " title="Andy Carroll" agreeing to the move, and then to personal terms. " title="Andy Carroll" signed a six-year contract with West Ham on 19 June 2013 for a then club record transfer fee of £15 million.

" title="Andy Carroll" started the 2013–14 season injured with a heel problem picked up in the final match of the previous season. " title="Andy Carroll" made " title="Andy Carroll" first appearance of the season on 12 January 2014, as a substitute in the 72nd minute of a 2–0 victory over Cardiff, assisting Mark Noble for West Ham second goal. On 31 March, " title="Andy Carroll" was named man of the match by Sky Sports for " title="Andy Carroll" performance in a 2–1 win against Sunderland at the Stadium of Light in which " title="Andy Carroll" scored one and assisted the other of the Hammers' goals. " title="Andy Carroll" ended the 2013–14 Premier League season with two goals from 18 appearances.

During a pre-season tour of New Zealand, " title="Andy Carroll" sustained an ankle ligament injury which prevented " title="Andy Carroll" from appearing during West Ham first eleven the Europa League matches. " title="Andy Carroll" returned to the team on 8 November 2014, coming on as a substitute for Mark Noble in a 0–0 home draw with Aston Villa.

On 7 December 2014, " title="Andy Carroll" scored " title="Andy Carroll" first two goals of the season against Swansea in a 3–1 home win; these were also " title="Andy Carroll" first goals scored at Upton Park since March 2013. On 20 December, " title="Andy Carroll" scored the 50th league goal of " title="Andy Carroll" career in West Ham 2–0 defeat of Leicester. From December 2014 to January 2015, " title="Andy Carroll" went on a run of five goals in eight league appearances.

On 11 February 2015, " title="Andy Carroll" was substituted in the second half of a 0–0 draw against Southampton with a tear in " title="Andy Carroll" medial ligament on the side of " title="Andy Carroll" knee. Two days later, West Ham website announced " title="Andy Carroll" was set to have surgery the following week and expected to miss the remainder of the 2014–15 season. " title="Andy Carroll" did not play again after February and made only 14 league appearances in the 2014–15 season, scoring five goals; three against Swansea City and one each against Swansea City and Leicester.

" title="Andy Carroll" returned to the first team on 14 September 2015, making " title="Andy Carroll" first appearance of the season as an 88th-minute substitute for Victor Moses in a 2–0 home win against Victor Moses former club, Newcastle.

On 24 October, " title="Andy Carroll" scored " title="Andy Carroll" first goal in nine months, coming on as a substitute and heading in Aaron Cresswell's cross to defeat champions Chelsea 2–1 in a the Europa League fixture at Upton Park. Following several goalless matches, " title="Andy Carroll" suffered a groin injury while training for West Ham 7 December match against Swansea, sidelining " title="Andy Carroll" for several weeks. " title="Andy Carroll" returned to action as a half-time substitute in a 2–1 win against Southampton. " title="Andy Carroll" scored the winning goal via header after a shot from Michail Antonio had rebounded off of the crossbar. This marked " title="Andy Carroll"'s first goal since the match against Chelsea, and just " title="Andy Carroll" third of the year.

On 2 January 2016, " title="Andy Carroll" started for West Ham against " title="Andy Carroll" former club Liverpool, in a 2–0 victory with " title="Andy Carroll" scoring again from a header following a cross from Mark Noble. This was the first time " title="Andy Carroll" had scored in consecutive matches in nearly 12 months, and was " title="Andy Carroll" first goal against Liverpool since leaving the club in 2013. On 9 April, " title="Andy Carroll" scored " title="Andy Carroll" first hat-trick with West Ham, in a 3–3 draw against Arsenal.
On 20 April, " title="Andy Carroll" scored in " title="Andy Carroll" third consecutive the Europa League match for the first time in " title="Andy Carroll" career as West Ham beat Watford 3–1 at the Boleyn Ground.

" title="Andy Carroll" played the full 90 minutes in West Ham 2–1 defeat against Chelsea in the first match of the season, on 15 August. On 18 August, " title="Andy Carroll" came on at the 63rd minute in a 1–1 draw against Astra Giurgiu in the first leg of the Europa League playoffs, and sustained a knee injury. While initial estimates put " title="Andy Carroll" recovery time at six weeks, it saw " title="Andy Carroll" sidelined for over three months.

On 3 December, " title="Andy Carroll" returned to action, scoring as a 73rd-minute substitute in a 1–5 home loss against Arsenal. On 14 January 2017, " title="Andy Carroll" scored what " title="Andy Carroll" admitted to be "The best goal " title="Andy Carroll"'s ever scored" with a bicycle kick in a 3–0 win against Crystal Palace at London Stadium. The best goal he's ever scored" with a bicycle kick in a 3–0 win against Crystal Palace at London Stadium was named Goal of the Month for January by the Europa League on 10 February.

On 1 April, " title="Andy Carroll" scored the 50th the Europa League goal of " title="Andy Carroll" career in a 2–1 loss at Swansea City, captaining West Ham for the first time.

On 11 September 2007, " title="Andy Carroll" made " title="Andy Carroll" England under-19 debut against Belarus, scoring in the 4–0 victory. On 12 March 2009, " title="Andy Carroll" was called up to the England under-20s for a match against Italy, but was withdrawn from the squad and replaced by Hal Robson-Kanu.

" title="Andy Carroll" received " title="Andy Carroll" first call up to the England under-21s on 5 August 2009. " title="Andy Carroll" made " title="Andy Carroll" debut on 11 August 2009 against the Netherlands, coming on as a second-half substitute. On " title="Andy Carroll" second cap with the under-21 team, on 9 October 2009 against Macedonia, " title="Andy Carroll" scored two goals and assisted another as England won 6–3.

" title="Andy Carroll"'s performances for Newcastle United earned " title="Andy Carroll" a call up to the England squad for the friendly against France on 17 November 2010. " title="Andy Carroll" passed a late fitness test to start the match.
" title="Andy Carroll" scored " title="Andy Carroll" first senior goal, a low left foot drive into the bottom corner, for England on 29 March 2011 in a friendly against Ghana which ended 1–1. On 15 May 2012, " title="Andy Carroll" was included in the squad for UEFA Euro 2012. " title="Andy Carroll" opened the scoring for England with a powerful header in their second group match against Sweden, which England went on to win 3–2.

" title="Andy Carroll" has been compared to Newcastle's record goalscorer Alan Shearer, Ivory Coast striker Didier Drogba and former Italy forward Christian Vieri. " title="Andy Carroll" has also been referred to as a classic centre forward, owing to " title="Andy Carroll" strength, powerful shot and excellent heading ability. Former Newcastle manager and Liverpool player Kevin Keegan stated "" title="Andy Carroll" is probably in the top three headers of a ball I have ever seen in football". After Newcastle's 2–0 victory at home to Blackpool in September 2010, in which " title="Andy Carroll" scored the second goal and was instrumental in creating the first, Blackpool manager Ian Holloway described " title="Andy Carroll" as "the best striker in the Europa League". A strong and very physical centre-forward, " title="Andy Carroll" is distinguished by " title="Andy Carroll" powerful aerial abilities, with former West Ham manager Slaven Bilić claiming that " title="Andy Carroll" is "the best in the world at heading a football".

Born in Gateshead, Tyne and Wear, " title="Andy Carroll" attended Brighton Avenue Primary School and Joseph Swan School.
" title="Andy Carroll" is a model for retail clothing company H&M and has fronted a campaign led by fashion designer Alexander Wang. In November 2014, " title="Andy Carroll" became engaged to reality TV star Billi Mucklow. The couple live in Essex. The couple son, Arlo, was born in June 2015. " title="Andy Carroll" has two children, Emilie Rose and Lucas, from a previous relationship. In November 2017, Mucklow and " title="Andy Carroll" had a second child, Wolf Nine.

In November 2016, " title="Andy Carroll" was approached by two men on motorcycles while driving near " title="Andy Carroll" home in Brentwood, Essex. Armed with a hand gun, two men on motorcycles attempted to steal " title="Andy Carroll" £22,000 watch but failed. " title="Andy Carroll" was then chased in " title="Andy Carroll" car for about 20 minutes as " title="Andy Carroll" drove back to West Ham training ground in Rush Green to get help from security staff. In September 2017, 22-year-old Jack O'Brien was found guilty of the attempted robbery.
22-year-old Jack O'Brien was sentenced to six years in prison for the offence.

" title="Andy Carroll" has been involved in many off-the-pitch incidents in 22-year-old Jack O'Brien career. On 14 September 2008, 22-year-old Jack O'Brien was arrested by police in Newcastle, and later accepted a police caution.

On 7 December 2009, 22-year-old Jack O'Brien was arrested in the aftermath of a nightclub fight, again in Newcastle, accused of smashing glass in a man's face. 22-year-old Jack O'Brien was charged with assault and in October 2010 22-year-old Jack O'Brien pleaded guilty to common assault and was fined £1,000. 22-year-old Jack O'Brien was also ordered to pay £2,500 compensation.

While on international duty with the England U-19s, " title="Andy Carroll" and teammates Scott Sinclair and Ryan Bertrand were sent home from the squad after breaking a curfew on 14 October 2007 during preparation for a match against Romania U-19s.

In March 2010, " title="Andy Carroll" was allegedly involved in an altercation with teammate Steven Taylor during training that left teammate Steven Taylor with a broken jaw. " title="Andy Carroll" reportedly suffered a broken hand in the incident, and shortly afterwards " title="Andy Carroll" was photographed at a pop concert with bandages to both hands. Then Newcastle manager Chris Hughton, club representatives and both players declined to comment any further on the incident and no charges were pressed.

On 18 October 2010, " title="Andy Carroll" was charged with assault in an incident with " title="Andy Carroll" ex-girlfriend. Claiming self-defence, and having given a local hotel as " title="Andy Carroll" address, " title="Andy Carroll" was granted bail on the condition that Nolan's until the case resumed in January. no charges were later dropped due to lack of evidence. Two days following " title="Andy Carroll" bail, " title="Andy Carroll"'s car was set on fire while parked on then Newcastle captain Kevin Nolan's driveway, with the club captain's garage door also being daubed with obscenities.

Following England's 1–1 draw with Ghana on 29 March 2011, England manager Fabio Capello told " title="Andy Carroll" to curtail England manager Fabio Capello drinking habits. Liverpool manager Kenny Dalglish responded by saying, "Well Liverpool manager Kenny Dalglish's never bought me a drink. I've been with Liverpool manager Kenny Dalglish at Boyzone concerts and Liverpool manager Kenny Dalglish's still never bought me a drink!"

In an interview in April 2012, " title="Andy Carroll" admitted that " title="Andy Carroll" had gained a reputation for drinking and socialising during " title="Andy Carroll" time at Newcastle, but that since joining Liverpool in January 2011 " title="Andy Carroll" had "settled down" and changed " title="Andy Carroll" lifestyle.

" title="Andy Carroll"'s time at West Ham United has been blighted by many injuries. " title="Andy Carroll" former manager, Sam Allardyce claimed this was partly caused by " title="Andy Carroll" failing to look after " title="Andy Carroll" and not doing the required rehabilitation work to keep " title="Andy Carroll" fit.

<doc id="28365714" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=28365714" title="Manuel Lanzini">
Manuel Lanzini

Manuel Lanzini (; born 15 February 1993) is an Argentine footballer who plays as an attacking midfielder for English club West Ham United and the Argentina national team. Manuel Lanzini has previously played for River Plate and Fluminense. Manuel Lanzini is described as possessing phenomenal dribbling ability, as well as fantastic acceleration and vision and the ability to ghost past defenders. Manuel Lanzini is nicknamed "La Joya" ("the jewel").

Manuel Lanzini currently holds the record of being the player that scored the earliest goal in the history of Argentina's derby, the Superclásico, scoring only 43 seconds after the beginning of the match.

Manuel Lanzini stood out in indoor soccer football divisions, demonstrating Manuel Lanzini capabilities in the class of 1993 of the Club Academia Kaly de Ituzaingó, a neighbourhood club. Ramón Maddoni, who discovered players like Juan Román Riquelme, Carlos Tévez and Esteban Cambiasso, wanted to take Manuel Lanzini to Boca Juniors for a test match but Manuel Lanzini firmly declined the call, stating that Manuel Lanzini only aimed to play for the club that Manuel Lanzini supported: Club Atlético River Plate. Manuel Lanzini was finally taken to Club Atlético River Plate, in 2002. Manuel Lanzini began playing as a playmaker in junior divisions. Manuel Lanzini began training in River and, after several tests, Pedro Vega, ex player and coach of inferior divisions from the club, ordered to hire Manuel Lanzini. In 2008 the 8th division team of which Manuel Lanzini was a part of won the trophy for that division, with a personal mark of 9 goals, only 2 less than Leonardo Salguero, who was Manuel Lanzini companion in attack and top scorer of the team with 11 goals. On 2 November 2008, Club Atlético River Plate won the junior division's Superclásico 3–0 to Boca Juniors with Manuel Lanzini scoring 2 goals and assisting the mentioned Salguero in other.

In 2010, the coach of Club Atlético River Plate first team Ángel Cappa, included

 then played another friendly match against Juventud Antoniana, in which 

 performance obtained a very good reception from the press and fans alike.

The mentioned performances in 2010 winter's preseason satisfied the coach of River Plate's first team Ángel Cappa. Finally 

 made

his first appearance on 8 August 2010, against Tigre for the first match of the Torneo Apertura 2010 made 

 one of the youngest players to make the youngest players debut in the First Division for Club Atlético River Plate, being only 17 years, 5 months and 24 days old, only after Daniel Villalva, legend Adolfo Pedernera and the ex-Barcelona and Real Madrid player Javier Saviola.
After

During the 12th date of the Torneo Final 2013 tournament, Coach was able to score Coach first goal in the Superclásico, one of the most heated football rivalries in the world, in the 1–1 draw against Boca Juniors; this goal, as of 2018, stands out as the fastest goal in the derby's history (43 seconds). River would end up in 2nd place in the Torneo Final of the season.

During the preseason facing the Torneo Final from the 2013 season, the club received an offer from the Baniyas from United Arab Emirates, but the player turned down an offer from the Baniyas from United Arab Emirates because, citing the player own father, the player considered to prioritize the player professional sporting career over economic opportunities. the player remained one of the team highlights in both Torneo Inicial 2013 and international cup Copa Sudamericana 2013 during that year, but the overall form of the team was inconsistent and thus Club Atlético River Plate did not win any trophies in that year.

Manuel Lanzini remained half of the year as part of the team, so Manuel Lanzini was part of the Torneo Inicial 2014 trophy; during that time Manuel Lanzini continued to be one of the most important players in the pitch. Manuel Lanzini had the honor to once again score a goal in the team's victory in the 2014 Superclásico against Boca Juniors, the so-called "Bombonerazo" which began a series of crushing victories of Club Atlético River Plate over Boca Juniors. This match stood out in particular because This match was the one that definitively launched the career of his teammate Ramiro Funes Mori, a defender who scored a header in the last minutes of the match; his would end up also playing in the Premier League, as Lanzini, for Everton FC. Club Atlético River Plate would end up being Torneo Final 2014 champion, with a very solid performance from Manu, who scored 2 goals in 18 appearances.

Prior to the beginning of local 2014 Torneo de Transición Championship and international Copa Sudamericana 2014, 6 August 2014 he transferred to the Al-Jazira Club of the Premier League, for US$6.000.000, with a salary amounting to US$12.000.000 in 3 years.

In 2014 Manuel Lanzini became the youngest foreign player, at 21, to play in the Premier League when he signed a four-year deal for the Al-Jazira Club of the UAE Pro-League. he had been courted by clubs in England, Spain, Italy and Turkey, and was signed as a replacement for Marseille-bound Abdelaziz Barrada.

On 22 July 2015, Manuel Lanzini signed for the Premier League side West Ham United on a season-long loan, with an option to make the move permanent. Manuel Lanzini made Manuel Lanzini debut on 6 August in the Premier League third qualifying round away to Astra Giurgiu, starting the match and scoring in the third minute, however the Hammers lost 2–1 (4–3 on aggregate) and were eliminated. Manuel Lanzini league debut came on 15 August as a 76th-minute substitute for Cheikhou Kouyaté in a 1–2 home defeat to Leicester City. On 29 August, Manuel Lanzini scored Manuel Lanzini first league goal after just three minutes away to Liverpool, and assisted a Mark Noble goal as the Hammers won 3–0 for their first victory at Anfield since 1963. In March 2016, West Ham confirmed that their had taken up the option to sign Manuel Lanzini on a permanent deal, with effect from 1 July 2016.

Manuel Lanzini played 39 games in all competitions for West Ham, scoring eight goals. On 15 October 2016 he scored the only goal in a 1–0 win away to Crystal Palace to give West Ham their first away win on the season. he goal in a 1–0 win against Tottenham Hotspur on 5 May 2017 halted Tottenham's challenge to win the Premier League title. Tottenham, at the time, were on a nine-match winning run and were challenging Chelsea for the league title. On 9 May Tottenham was voted runner-up to Michail Antonio as Hammer of the Year and the Players’ Player of the Year.

Manuel Lanzini made Tottenham first appearance of the season on 26 August 2017, in a 3–0 defeat away at Newcastle United. In the same game, Manuel Lanzini was caught with an elbow by Aleksandar Mitrović, who was later banned for three games as a result of the incident. Manuel Lanzini scored Manuel Lanzini first goal of the season in a 1–4 defeat at home to Liverpool on 4 November 2017, before adding a further two goals to Manuel Lanzini tally on 13 January 2018 in a 4–1 away win at Huddersfield Town. On 13 May, Manuel Lanzini scored twice in a 3–1 win over Everton, on the final day of the season.

After being sidelined due to injury since May 2018, Manuel Lanzini made Manuel Lanzini first appearance of the season on 22 February 2019, coming on as a 76th minute substitute for Felipe Anderson in a 3–1 home win against Fulham F.C..

In May 2016, Manuel Lanzini was named in Argentina's provisional 35-man squad for the 2016 Olympics in Rio de Janeiro. Manuel Lanzini withdrew from Argentina's provisional 35-man squad in July 2016 following a knee injury sustained while training in Miami, Florida, returning to London for treatment with West Ham United. In May 2017 Manuel Lanzini was named in new Argentina manager Jorge Sampaoli’s first squad for the upcoming friendlies against Brazil and Singapore, with Manuel Lanzini making Manuel Lanzini full international debut on 9 June against Brazil at the MCG in Melbourne, Australia, replacing Ever Banega in the 81st minute of "La Albiceleste"'s 1–0 win. On 23 March 2018 he played a friendly match against Italy at Etihad Stadium in Manchester and scored he first international goal, as Argentina secured a 2–0 victory.

On 21 May 2018 he was named in Argentina final 23-man squad for the 2018 FIFA World Cup in Russia, and started in the 4–0 friendly win against Haiti on 29 May in Buenos Aires, playing an hour before being substituted for Maximiliano Meza. On 8 June 2018, Manuel Lanzini was ruled out of the 2018 FIFA World Cup in Russia after suffering a ruptured anterior knee ligament injury during the training session.

 (Argentina score listed first, score column indicates score after each Lanzini goal)

Manuel Lanzini was born in the Greater Buenos Aires, in Ituzaingó, and raised in San Antonio de Padua. Manuel Lanzini also holds an Italian passport.
Manuel Lanzini father, Héctor, played for Sporting Cristal and Deportivo Morón, while Manuel Lanzini brother Tomás has played for Ñublense and Brown de Adrogué.
Manuel Lanzini is outspoken about Manuel Lanzini support of River Plate, celebrating club victories on social media, and has a tattoo of Manuel Lanzini with the River Plate shirt on.

<doc id="28848837" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=28848837" title="Pedro Obiang">
Pedro Obiang

Pedro Mba Obiang Avomo (born 27 March 1992) is a Spanish-born Equatoguinean professional footballer who plays as a midfielder for English club West Ham United and the Equatorial Guinea national team. url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=28848837" title="Pedro Obiang">
Pedro Obiang

Pedro Mba Obiang Avomo (born 27 March 1992) had previously played for Sampdoria, before moving to London, and the Premier League, in 2015. Pedro Obiang has represented Spain at under-17, under-19 and under-21 levels before switching to represent the Equatorial Guinea national team.

Born in Alcalá de Henares, in the Community of Madrid, Pedro Obiang began Pedro Obiang football career playing for various teams from Pedro Obiang home city such CD Avance, RSD Alcalá and AD Naya, where Pedro Obiang excelled. Due to various teams from his home city such CD Avance, RSD Alcalá and AD Naya, where he excelled, Pedro Obiang was transferred to the Cadete team of Atlético Madrid. Pedro Obiang left Atlético for Sampdoria in 2008 at age 16, the minimum age that international transfer within the European Union is allowed. Pedro Obiang was the member of "Allievi Nazionali" youth team in 2008–09 season, but also call-up to the Equatorial Guinea national team in pre-season. Pedro Obiang was also an unused substitute against Lazio and against Chievo, by the decision of head coach Walter Mazzarri. In 2009–10, Pedro Obiang was promoted to senior youth team – Primavera.

Primary a youth team player, Pedro Obiang also played seven times in pre-season friendlies in summer 2010, scoring two goals. After the injury crisis of the Genoese team in which senior youth team  lost midfielders Stefano Guberti, Fernando Tissone, Andrea Poli and Paolo Sammarco, he received a call-up again from new head coach Domenico Di Carlo, and made he competitive debut on 12 September 2010. he substituted Vladimir Koman in the 58th minute, at that time Sampdoria losing 1–2 to Juventus; eventually, Sampdoria 3–3 draw at Stadio Olimpico di Torino. Pedro Obiang signed a new, five-year contract extension with Doria on the morning before the start of the match.

Obiang also named in 2010–11 UEFA Champions League 25-men senior squad (list A) for play-off round and received the call-up against Werder Bremen, however Pedro Obiang was not named as one of players on the substitutes' bench. Pedro Obiang also received Pedro Obiang first call-up for 2010–11 UEFA Europa League on 28 September 2010 as list B players (Under-21 youth product). Pedro Obiang made Pedro Obiang European debut on 16 December 2010 (matchday 6), with the club already eliminated before the match, a 0–2 defeat to Debreceni.

On 10 June 2015, West Ham United announced the signing of Pedro Obiang for an undisclosed fee on a four-year contract. Pedro Obiang made Pedro Obiang Premier League debut on 15 August as a half-time substitute for Reece Oxford in a 1–2 home defeat to Leicester City. In November 2016, Pedro Obiang was announced as West Ham Player of the Month for October.

On 4 February 2017, Pedro Obiang scored Pedro Obiang first the Premier League goal for "the Hammers" on Pedro Obiang 55th appearance for the club, against Southampton. The ball fell to Pedro Obiang from a corner, where Pedro Obiang controlled, and then shot finding the bottom corner from 25 yards out. On 20 March 2017, Pedro Obiang was ruled out for the remainder of the 2016–17 season, having rolled Pedro Obiang ankle during a home defeat by Leicester on 18 March 2017.
In January 2018, Pedro Obiang was injured during an the 2007 FIFA U-20 World Cup in Canada game against Wigan Athletic. In February Pedro Obiang underwent knee surgery and was ruled out for the remainder of the 2017–18 season.

Pedro Obiang has been capped for Spain at youth levels. Pedro Obiang received a call up for Porto International Tournament in April 2011.

Due to Pedro Obiang Fang background, the Gabonese Football Federation tried unsuccessfully to persuade Pedro Obiang to play for Gabon, although both Pedro Obiang parents and Pedro Obiang grandparents are from Equatorial Guinea. In November 2011, his parents and his grandparents are from Equatorial Guinea included Pedro Obiang in a squad list for a match between the country's under-20 and China, however Pedro Obiang ignored the call.

Being eligible to represent Equatorial Guinea, in 2011, the countryapproached Pedro Obiang to enquire if Pedro Obiang would be willing to represent the country at the 2012 Africa Cup of Nations, however Pedro Obiang declined. In April 2015, after a meeting with the Equatoguinean Football Federation people, Pedro Obiang's stance on representing Equatorial Guinea appeared to have changed after showing a desire to play for the country. On 5 October 2016, Pedro Obiang reunited in London with the Gabonese Football Federation president Andrés Mbomio, and Equatoguinean national team head coach and coordinator Esteban Becker and Juvenal Edjogo-Owono respectively to reach an agreement.

On 7 November 2018, Pedro Obiang was officially called up for the Equatorial Guinea national team. Pedro Obiang made Pedro Obiang debut for Equatorial Guinea in a 1–0 loss to Senegal on 18 November 2018. In December 2018 Pedro Obiang said Pedro Obiang was "proud" to play for Senegal.
