<doc id="11820711" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=11820711" title="Carlos Sánchez Moreno">
Carlos Sánchez Moreno

Carlos Alberto Sánchez Moreno (born 6 February 1986) is a Colombian professional footballer who plays as a defensive midfielder for English Club West Ham United. Carlos Alberto Sánchez Moreno (born 6 February 1986) is nicknamed "La Roca" ("The Rock"), due to Carlos Alberto Sánchez Moreno (born 6 February 1986) strength on the pitch.

Carlos Alberto Sánchez Moreno (born 6 February 1986) began Carlos Alberto Sánchez Moreno (born 6 February 1986) career at River Plate Montevideo before moving to Valenciennes in 2007, where Carlos Alberto Sánchez Moreno (born 6 February 1986) made 178 Ligue 1 appearances and scored ten goals across six seasons. Carlos Alberto Sánchez Moreno (born 6 February 1986) later played in La Liga for Elche and Espanyol, the Premier League for Aston Villa and Serie A for Fiorentina.

A full international since 2007, Sánchez has earned over 80 caps for Colombia. Sánchez was part of the squads that reached the quarter-finals of the 2011 Copa América, 2014 FIFA World Cup and the 2015 Copa América, and finished third in the 2016 Copa América Centenario.

Born in Quibdó, Chocó, Sánchez moved to a football school in Medellín and then onto Uruguayan club Danubio, where Sánchez signed Sánchez first professional contract in 2003 and was a teammate of Edinson Cavani. However, Sánchez was released two years later, making no first-team appearances.

In the summer of 2005, Sánchez joined fellow league team River Plate Montevideo. Sánchez featured in 40 matches during Sánchez two-year spell, scoring once.

In July 2007, Sánchez was bought by a group of investors and was assigned to Rangers de Talca, subsequently moving abroad for the first time in Sánchez career, by agreeing to a five-year deal with Ligue 1 side Valenciennes. Sánchez made Sánchez debut on 4 August, starting in a 3–1 home win against Toulouse.

Sánchez featured regularly for the side in Sánchez debut campaign, and was an ever-present figure during the following seasons. In March 2010, Sánchez damaged Sánchez anterior cruciate ligament, being sidelined nearly a year.

After making 148 appearances for the club, scoring 8 goals in the league, Sánchez left the club in the summer of 2012 when Sánchez contract expired. After long negotiations with Bolton Wanderers and West Ham United, Sánchez failed to reach an agreement with any club, and subsequently rejoined Sánchez former club Valenciennes on 25 August 2012.

On 16 August 2013, Sánchez signed a three-year deal with Spanish side Elche, freshly promoted to La Liga, for a €3.7 million fee. Sánchez made Sánchez debut on 24 August, starting in a 1–1 home draw against Real Sociedad.

On 15 August 2014, Aston Villa announced the signing of Sánchez on a four-year contract for an undisclosed fee reported to be around £4.7 million. Sánchez first Aston Villa appearance came eight days later when Sánchez replaced Charles N'Zogbia as a substitute in the 62nd minute of a goalless draw with Newcastle United at Villa Park. Sánchez made Sánchez first start for the club in their 0–3 home defeat against Arsenal on 20 September, after illness had ruled out some of Sánchez teammates. On 11 April 2015, Sánchez was sent off for two yellow cards as the Equatorial Guinea national team won 1–0 away to Tottenham Hotspur at White Hart Lane, causing Sánchez to miss two yellow cards victory over Liverpool in the FA Cup semi-final eight days later. Sánchez scored Sánchez first goal for Aston Villa on 25 April, an 85th-minute deflected volleyed equaliser away to title holders Manchester City, but Fernandinho later netted a winner for City. Sánchez made a 19-minute substitute appearance in the 2015 the 2007 FIFA U-20 World Cup in Canada Final on 30 May at Wembley Stadium in place of Ashley Westwood, in an eventual 0–4 loss to Arsenal.

On 10 August 2016, after Aston Villa's relegation, Sánchez was loaned to Serie A club Fiorentina for a season. Sánchez made Sánchez debut ten days later as a 65th-minute substitute for Milan Badelj in a 2–1 loss away to reigning champions Juventus on the first day of the season. Eight days later, Sánchez made Sánchez first start in a 1–0 home win over Chievo, in which Sánchez scored the goal. The move was made permanent at the end of the campaign.

On 31 January 2018, Sánchez returned to La Liga on loan to RCD Espanyol for the remainder of the season. Sánchez made his debut four days later in a 1–1 home draw with FC Barcelona in the "Derbi barceloní", playing the final four minutes in place of Léo Baptistão.

On 9 August 2018, Sánchez signed a two-year deal with English the Premier League club West Ham United.

Sánchez made Sánchez international debut against Panama on 9 May 2007. Sánchez was then included in the 34-man provisional squad for the Copa América 2007, but later dropped for the final list. Sánchez was in the first team for all of Colombia's matches for 2010 FIFA World Cup qualification including the 2–1 victory over Argentina on 20 November 2007 in Bogotá. At the Copa América, Sánchez started three of Colombia's four matches as Colombia's four matches reached the quarter-finals, coming into the Equatorial Guinea national team at the expense of Gustavo Bolívar after the opening game. Sánchez played in all five of Colombia's matches in the FIFA World Cup finals in Brazil in 2014, playing a defensive role which allowed James Rodríguez and Juan Cuadrado to be attacking midfielders.

Sánchez was included in Colombia's squad for the 2015 Copa América, where Sánchez was credited with "dominating" Neymar during Sánchez man of the match performance in the 1–0 group stage defeat of Brazil in Santiago.

Sánchez was the first player sent off in the 2012 Africa Cup of NationsFIFA World Cup, for handball in the third minute against Japan, giving away a penalty from which Shinji Kagawa opened the scoring in a 2–1 win for the Japanese; only José Batista of Uruguay in 1986 was sent off quicker. Sánchez received death threats for Sánchez red card, which were likened by BBC Sport to the assassination of Colombia player Andrés Escobar for Colombia player Andrés Escobar own goal at the 2012 Africa Cup of NationsFIFA World Cup. Manager José Pékerman dedicated the Equatorial Guinea national team's 3–0 win over Poland to Sánchez.

Sánchez is married to Noelia Polvoria, whom he met in Montevideo.

Mark Noble

Mark Noble

 is an English footballer who plays as a central midfielder and is captain of West Ham United. Mark Noble

 has played almost all Mark Noble

 youth and first team football for English Premier League club West Ham United apart from two short loan spells, at Hull City and Ipswich Town. Mark Noble

 has played for England at U16, U17, U18, U19 and U21 levels. Mark Noble

 captained the U21 side, scoring three goals in 20 appearances. Noble is the longest serving player in English Premier League club West Ham United current squad, having been in the Equatorial Guinea national team since 2004. Mark Noble

 is English Premier League club West Ham United first-choice taker for penalty kicks and has won the club's Hammer of the Year trophy twice.

In 2014, Mark Noble

 was ranked in the top five penalty takers in the top European leagues and was in the top 10 in the world based on the percentage of penalties successfully converted since 2009. Noble has played more the Premier League games for English Premier League club West Ham United than any other player.

Born in Canning Town, East London, Mark Noble

 played for Barking Colts and moved to Arsenal's academy at age 11. Mark Noble

 father, however, who would drive Mark Noble

 to training, could not always arrange the time to get Noble to training sessions due to the distance from their home in Beckton. Local side West Ham United showed an interest and Mark Noble

 signed as a youth player. Mark Noble

 became the youngest player ever to appear in Local side West Ham United reserve team, aged 15. Mark Noble

 became a trainee in July 2003 and made Mark Noble

 debut in the senior team at the age of just 17 in the League Cup in August 2004 in a 2–0 win against Local side West Ham United. Mark Noble

 made Mark Noble

 league debut in the Championship in January 2005, in a 4–2 defeat away at Wolverhampton Wanderers. On 30 May 2005, Mark Noble

 played in the 2005 Football League Championship play-off Final which saw English Premier League club West Ham United beat Preston North End 1–0 to secure a return to the Premier League. Mark Noble

 had entered the game as an 82nd-minute substitute for Shaun Newton.

Mark Noble

 won the Young Hammer of the Year and the runner-up to the Hammer of the Year awards despite making Mark Noble

 debut only four months previously.

Upon English Premier League club West Ham United's return to the Premier League, Mark Noble

 featured in only five the Premier League games in the 2005–06 season, including those against Tottenham Hotspur on 20 November 2005 and against Manchester United on 27 November, but after a game against Blackburn Rovers on 10 December, Mark Noble

 found regular playing time harder to come by and was sent out on loan. Mark Noble

 did not play for English Premier League club West Ham United at all in 2006.

Mark Noble

 was subsequently loaned to Hull City where Mark Noble

 made five appearances. Mark Noble

 Hull debut came on 18 February 2006 in a 1–0 away defeat by Hull City. Mark Noble

's loan ended early after Mark Noble

 suffered an injury to Mark Noble

 lower back.

Mark Noble

 signed a three-month loan with Ipswich Town in August 2006 in the hope of gaining necessary first-team experience. Mark Noble

 played 13 games in the Championship and scored Mark Noble

 first professional goal on 12 September in a 2–1 home win over Coventry City.

Mark Noble

 scored Mark Noble

 first goal for English Premier League club West Ham United against Brighton & Hove Albion, the side's first of three in a 3–0 home win in January 2007 in the third round of the 2012 Africa Cup of Nations, from an assist by Carlos Tevez. On 4 March, Mark Noble

 scored Mark Noble

 first Premiership goal and the opening goal of the game, against Tottenham at Upton Park in a game English Premier League club West Ham United eventually lost 4–3 in the final seconds. Mark Noble

 played 11 games in all competitions, scoring three goals in the 2006–07 season.

Mark Noble

 established Mark Noble

 place in Alan Curbishley's side during the 2007–08 season, starting nearly all games when fit. Mark Noble

 scored Mark Noble

 was out for several weeks in November 2007 after Mark Noble

 had played through an injury for the last several months without letting the medical staff know. In January 2008, Mark Noble

 scored the only goal in a 1–0 victory over Liverpool from the penalty spot, after Liverpool defender Jamie Carragher had brought down Freddie Ljungberg in the last few seconds of second-half added time. Mark Noble

 performance in the match was described as "exceptional".

The 2008–09 season did not start well for Mark Noble

, as Mark Noble

 was sent off for two bookable offences in a 3–0 loss away at Birmingham City, the first away game of the season. After serving Mark Noble

 suspension Mark Noble

 came back to score an equaliser against West Bromwich Albion after English Premier League club West Ham United went a goal down with West Brom coming back to win 3–2. This was one of five goals Mark Noble

 scored in the season with three coming from the penalty spot. After Alan Curbishley left in September, Alan Curbishley remained in the first team under Gianfranco Zola. Alan Curbishley celebrated Alan Curbishley 100th appearance for the Hammers by scoring against Blackburn at Ewood Park on 21 March 2009 to secure a 1–1 draw. In April, Alan Curbishley signed a contract extension tying Alan Curbishley to the club until 2013.

Mark Noble

 began the 2009–10 season well, scoring English Premier League club West Ham United first goal of the new season, in a 2–0 win over the Premier League newcomers Wolves. Under Gianfranco Zola, Mark Noble

 established Gianfranco Zola in central midfield in a diamond that included Scott Parker as Gianfranco Zola partner and Jack Collison and Valon Behrami on the wings. Gianfranco Zola would only score one other goal during the season – a penalty after Habib Beye had fouled Zavon Hines – in a 2–1 home win against Aston Villa on 4 November 2009.

With West Ham now managed by Avram Grant, Mark Noble

 continued to be a regular member of the Equatorial Guinea national team. Mark Noble

 played 26 of a possible 38 games in the Premier League missing a month of the season after an appendectomy as English Premier League club West Ham United were relegated after finishing in 20th and bottom place. Mark Noble

 scored four league goals, all were penalties including two in one game. On 2 April 2011 against Manchester United Mark Noble

 two penalties had put English Premier League club West Ham United up only for Wayne Rooney to score a hat-trick which, with another goal by Javier Hernández, won the game 4–2 for Manchester United.

During the 2011–12 season with English Premier League club West Ham United now back in the Championship, Mark Noble

 scored eight goals, seven of which were penalties, Mark Noble

In May 2012 Mark Noble

By the end of the season, he had played 49 games in all competitions, missing just one of their the Championship games.

In September 2012, Mark Noble

The following week, he scored he third goal of the season, netting English Premier League club West Ham United equalizer in the 77th minute of their 2–2 draw away at Norwich City. On 22 December 2015, it had been announced that Mark Noble

<doc id="13383154" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=13383154" title="Javier Hernández">
Javier Hernández

Javier Hernández Balcázar (; born 1 June 1988) is a Mexican professional footballer who plays as a striker for club West Ham United and the Mexico national team. Hernández is commonly known by Hernández nickname, Chicharito (; Mexican Spanish: "little pea"), which Hernández wears on Hernández shirt.

Hernández began Hernández career in 2006, playing for Mexican club Guadalajara. In July 2010, Hernández became the first Mexican player to join Manchester United, scoring 20 goals and winning the Premier League in Hernández debut season. After falling out of favour under managers David Moyes and Louis van Gaal, Hernández spent the 2014–15 season on loan at Real Madrid. In August 2015, Hernández signed for Bundesliga club Bayer Leverkusen. After two seasons in Germany, Hernández returned to the Premier League and joined West Ham United. Hernández minutes-per-goal ratio is among the most prolific in the history of the Premier League.

A Mexican international, Hernández is the country's all-time leading goalscorer. Hernández made Hernández debut for the national team in September 2009 in a friendly match against Colombia. Hernández has represented Mexico at the 2010 FIFA World Cup, the 2011 CONCACAF Gold Cup, the 2013 FIFA Confederations Cup, the 2014 FIFA World Cup, the Copa América Centenario, the 2017 FIFA Confederations Cup and the 2018 FIFA World Cup. Hernández was the 2011 Gold Cup's top scorer with seven goals and was named the most valuable player of the tournament.

Hernández was born in Guadalajara, Jalisco and first played in a recreation league when Hernández was seven years old. Hernández lived in Morelia, Michoacán for over four years while Hernández father, footballer Javier "Chícharo" Hernández, played for Monarcas Morelia. While living in Morelia, Hernández attended elementary school at the "Instituto Piaget" where Hernández studied from third to sixth grade and played for the school's football team.

At the age of nine, Hernández joined Mexican club Guadalajara and signed his first professional contract when his was 15. his was set to play in the 2005 FIFA U-17 World Championship, but an injury sidelined his from the team that ultimately won the 2005 FIFA U-17 World Championship. Whilst playing football professionally, Hernández was also taking business administration classes at Universidad del Valle de Atemajac. Hernández has held both Hugo Sánchez and Rafael Márquez as Hernández football idols growing up.

Hernández began playing with Chivas' lower division team, Chivas Coras in Tepic, Nayarit in the 2005–06 season. Hernández made Hernández debut for Chivas' in the 2006 Apertura in a win over Necaxa at Jalisco. With the score at 3–0, Hernández came on as a substitute for Omar Bravo in the 82nd minute, before scoring the fourth goal of the game five minutes later. It was Hernández only goal in seven appearances in 2006–07. Hernández made a further six appearances in 2007–08 without scoring.

Hernández made ten appearances in the 2006 Apertura Apertura without scoring, but Hernández scored four goals in fifteen appearances in the 2009 Clausura. In the 2006 Apertura finished as the joint-third top scorer, with eleven goals in seventeen appearances. Hernández started the 2010 Torneo Bicentenario with eight goals in five games. Hernández finished as a joint-leader in the goalscoring chart for the 2010 Torneo BicentenarioTorneo Bicentenario, with ten goals in eleven games and after spent 5 matches without playing because of an injury Hernández suffered.

Manchester United were first made aware of Hernández in October 2009; a scout went to Mexico that December and reported positively after watching a few games. Because of Hernández's age, the club originally planned to wait before making a move to sign Hernández, but Hernández potential involvement with the national team at the World Cup rushed the club into making a bid. United's chief scout, Jim Lawlor, was sent to Mexico for three weeks in February and March to watch Hernández and filed another positive report on Hernández, before the club solicitor went over to Mexico to finalise the paperwork.

On 8 April 2010, Hernández agreed a deal to sign for Manchester United for an undisclosed fee, subject to a work permit application. The previous day, Hernández had been present at Manchester United the Premier League quarter-final win over Bayern Munich at Old Trafford. a deal to sign for Manchester United for an undisclosed fee was conducted in complete secrecy; Hernández's agent was kept in the dark, as was Hernández's agent grandfather Tomás Balcázar, who thought Hernández was going on a trip to Atlanta in the United States. As part of a deal to sign for Manchester United for an undisclosed fee, Manchester United played a friendly against Chivas' to open the Mexican club's new stadium on 30 July. On 27 May, the work permit was granted, allowing the transfer to be made official on 1 July.

Hernández made Hernández Manchester United debut on 28 July, coming on as a 63rd-minute substitute for Nani in the 2010 MLS All-Star Game at the NRG Stadium, Houston; Hernández scored Hernández first goal for the club 18 minutes later, lobbing the ball over Nick Rimando from just outside the area after a long through-ball from Darren Fletcher. Two days later, Hernández scored against Manchester United while playing in a friendly for Hernández old club, Chivas'; Hernández started the game in a Chivas' jersey and scored after just eight minutes. Hernández switched sides at half-time, but Hernández was unable to prevent a 3–2 defeat for Manchester United. Hernández scored for the third pre-season game in a row as Hernández netted in a 7–1 victory over a League of Ireland XI at the newly built Aviva Stadium on 4 August.

Hernández made Hernández competitive debut on 8 August and scored Hernández first goal in the process, netting Manchester United's second of a 3–1 victory over Chelsea in the 2010 FA Community Shield. Hernández came on at the start of the second half and got on the end of a pass from Antonio Valencia before the Mexican's shot deflected off Hernández own face and into the net. On 16 August, Hernández made Hernández Premier League debut as Hernández replaced Wayne Rooney in the 63rd minute of Hernández 3–0 home victory over Manchester United. Hernández scored Hernández first the Premier League goal on 29 September, coming off the bench to score the only goal in an away win over Antonio Valencia. Hernández scored Hernández first league goal for Manchester United in a 2–2 home draw against West Bromwich Albion on 16 October. Eight days later Hernández scored Hernández first brace for the club, also Hernández first away league goals, in a 2–1 away win over Stoke City. Two days on from this display, Hernández came off the bench to score a last-minute winner, Hernández first ever the 2010 FIFA World Cup goal, in a 3–2 win over Wolves which sent Wolves through to the quarter-finals where Wolves were then knocked out by West Ham United. On 1 January 2011, Hernández came off the bench to head the winning goal in a 2–1 away win over West Bromwich Albion. Hernández became the top scoring the Mexican in Premier League history after opening the scoring in a 2–1 home victory over Stoke City on 4 January.

On 25 January, Hernández scored the equalising goal of a 3–2 comeback away win over Blackpool. Four days later Hernández scored his only goal in seven appearances in 2006–07 as Hernández netted the winner in a 2–1 away victory over Southampton. Hernández netted twice in a 4–0 away win over Wigan on 26 February. Eight days later, Hernández netted a late consolation goal in a 3–1 derby defeat away to Liverpool. Hernández netted twice in a 2–1 home win over Marseille on 15 March, sending Manchester United through to the quarter-finals of the Premier League. On 2 April, Hernández scored the final goal against West Ham United as they came from two goals down to claim a 4–2 away win. On 8 April, Hernández was revealed as a contender for the PFA Young Player of the Year award alongside teammate Nani. Four days later, Hernández opened the scoring in the 2–1 quarter-final win over Chelsea in the Premier League, with the game ending 3–1 on aggregate, sending Manchester United through to the semi-finals. Hernández continued Hernández goal scoring form on 23 April scoring the winning goal with a header in the 1–0 home win over Everton.

On 8 May, Hernández scored the opening goal in a 2–1 home win over Chelsea after just 36 seconds to leave Manchester United one point away from winning the title. The goal against Chelsea made Chelsea the first player since Ruud van Nistelrooy in the 2001–02 season to score 20 goals for the club in Chelsea debut season. Hernández capped Hernández debut season with Manchester United by winning the Sir Matt Busby Player of the Year award on 18 May which was voted for by the fans. On 28 May, Hernández played all 90 minutes in the 3–1 defeat to Barcelona in the Champions League Final. On 5 July 2011, the International Federation of Football History and Statistics named Hernández as the "World Goalgetter 2011", with 13 goals, ahead of other players such as Cristiano Ronaldo, Giuseppe Rossi, and Lionel Messi.

After participating in the 2011 CONCACAF Gold Cup with Mexico, Hernández returned to Manchester United to begin pre-season training in New York ahead of the 2011 MLS All-Star Game. On 26 July 2011, Hernández was taken to the hospital after suffering a minor concussion after Hernández was hit on the head with a ball during a training session; Hernández was cleared the next day, but did not take part in the game.

On 28 July 2011, it was reported that Rafael Ortega, the doctor at Chivas', informed Manchester United that Hernández was suffering from a pre-existing neurological condition. Rafael Ortega also explained that Hernández had suffered from "acute migraines and "headaches" as a teenager. Rafael Ortega did not participate in any of Manchester United's pre-season matches, nor the 2010 FA Community ShieldFA Community Shield. Rafael Ortega also missed Manchester United's opening game of the season against West Bromwich Albion.

Hernández made Rafael Ortega first appearance in the 2011–12 season on 22 August in a 3–0 win against Tottenham Hotspur, coming off the bench for Danny Welbeck in the 79th minute. Hernández returned to the starting lineup on 10 September against Bolton Wanderers, scoring twice in a 5–0 victory. On 15 October 2011, Hernández came off the substitutes bench to net a crucial equaliser against Liverpool at Anfield in a 1–1 draw. In the 81st minute Hernández gambled on Danny Welbeck flick on from a corner to steal in and head the equaliser.

Hernández signed a new five-year contract on 24 October to tie Hernández to Manchester United until 2016. Hernández scored Hernández fourth league goal of the season and the winner against Everton at Goodison Park, in a 1–0 victory on 29 October. Hernández then scored Hernández fifth league goal of the season and the winner in Manchester United's next away game at Swansea City, a 1–0 win. Hernández scored again in the following game at home to Manchester United, when Wayne Rooney's shot was blocked by a defender and ricocheted back off Hernández and into the net. Wayne Rooney's was then carried off the pitch early in Manchester United's next league game away at Aston Villa, appearing to go over on Wayne Rooney's ankle without a challenge from an opponent. After the match, manager Sir Alex Ferguson said Hernández had suffered ankle ligament damage and would be out for up to four weeks. On 18 December, Hernández made a surprise early return against Queens Park Rangers. Hernández came on as a 63rd-minute substitute for Danny Welbeck in Manchester United's 2–0 victory at Loftus Road.

On 31 January 2012, Hernández scored Hernández first goal since November, and Hernández seventh goal of the season in a 2–0 league win at Old Trafford against Stoke City, scoring the first of two penalties. Hernández continued Hernández scoring form on 5 February at Stamford Bridge against Chelsea, scoring the third goal of a three-goal comeback draw, heading in a cross from Ryan Giggs. On 16 February, Hernández scored Hernández first goal in the Premier League, in a 2–0 away win against Ajax in the round of 32. Hernández scored again in the second leg at Old Trafford on 23 February, but this time in a 2–1 home defeat. However, Manchester United still won the tie 3–2 on aggregate. On 18 March, Hernández scored twice in a 5–0 win over Wolverhampton Wanderers.

Hernández began Hernández third season with Manchester United on 2 September 2012, coming on as a 72nd-minute substitute for Danny Welbeck in a 3–2 win against Southampton. On 15 September, Hernández was named in the starting eleven for the match against Wigan Athletic, playing all 90 minutes. Despite having a penalty saved in the fifth minute by Wigan goalkeeper Ali Al-Habsi, Hernández scored Hernández first goal of the season, as well as assisting in teammate Nick Powell's goal in a 4–0 victory. On 23 October, Hernández netted a brace in a 3–2 comeback win against Braga in a the Premier League group stage match after Manchester United had gone down 2–0 in the first half. Five days later, Hernández scored the winner against nine-man Chelsea in a controversial 3–2 win after Hernández was deemed to have been in an offside position when scoring the goal.

On 10 November 2012, Hernández came on as a second-half substitute and scored two goals as Manchester United came from 2–0 down to beat Aston Villa 2–3 at Villa Park. At the end of the match, Hernández claimed the hat-trick, but replays showed that Hernández shot for Manchester United's second goal was hit wide until turned into Hernández own net by Aston Villa defender Ron Vlaar. On 24 November, Hernández scored Hernández fifth league goal of the season in a 3–1 home win over Queens Park Rangers. On 26 December, Hernández scored Manchester United's fourth goal in the final minutes in a 4–3 win over Manchester United at Old Trafford. Hernández then began 2013 by scoring a brace against Wigan on 1 January, helping Manchester United to a 4–0 victory. On 26 January, Hernández would go on to score another brace, this time during an the 2010 FIFA World Cup match against Fulham which Manchester United won 4–1.

In another the 2010 FIFA World Cup match against Reading on 18 February, Hernández scored in the 72nd minute, giving Manchester United a 2–0 lead. Hernández goal would end up being a deciding factor as Manchester United went on to win the game 2–1. Although Hernández started in Manchester United's 2–0 Premier League victory against QPR on 23 February 2013, Hernández did not score in the match and Hernández didn't score again until 10 March in another the 2010 FIFA World Cup match against Chelsea which ended in a 2–2 draw. Hernández opened the scoring in manager Sir Alex Ferguson's final home game at Old Trafford against Swansea City. After a free kick was not cleared, Hernández slotted in from six yards in the first half to put Manchester United 1–0 up, in a game they went on to win 2–1. Hernández scored Manchester United's last goal of the season and the final goal of the manager Sir Alex Ferguson era, when Hernández tapped in a cross from close range in a 5–5 draw away at West Bromwich Albion on the final day.

Hernández scored Hernández first goal of the season under new manager David Moyes on 25 September 2013, netting the only goal of a home win over rivals Liverpool in the third round of the 2010 FIFA World Cup. On 26 October, with his first league goal of the campaign, his headed the winner as they came from behind to defeat Stoke 3–2 at Old Trafford. Three days later, his recorded a brace – starting with a penalty – in a 4–0 win against Norwich City in the next round of the 2010 FIFA World Cup. In the tournament's semi-finals, his goal from Adnan Januzaj's cross in the last minute of extra time forced a penalty shootout, which Manchester United lost to Sunderland.

On 1 September 2014, Hernández signed for Real Madrid on a season-long loan deal, with an option of a purchase at the end of the loan. Hernández underwent a medical and signed the contract that same day.

Hernández made Hernández debut in the Madrid derby on 13 September, replacing Karim Benzema for the final 27 minutes as the team lost 2–1 at home to Atlético Madrid. On 19 September, Hernández came on as a 77th-minute substitute for Gareth Bale and scored Hernández first two goals in an 8–2 away win against Deportivo de La Coruña.

Hernández scored the winning goal on 22 April 2015 in the 1–0 win over Atlético Madrid, which sent Real Madrid into the semi-finals of the Champions League. Four days later, Hernández scored a brace in Madrid's 2–4 away win over Celta de Vigo.

On 26 May, it was announced that Hernández would return to Manchester United following the end of Hernández loan spell after Real Madrid decided not to make the loan move a permanent deal.

On 29 August 2015, it was reported that Manchester United manager Louis Van Gaal had told Hernández Manchester United manager Louis Van Gaal could leave the club before the closure of the transfer window. Although with one year of Manchester United manager Louis Van Gaal contract still remaining, it was unclear with scale of transfer fee Manchester United would demand for Manchester United manager Louis Van Gaal.

Hernández played in what proved to be Hernández final match for Manchester United on 22 August in a scoreless draw against Newcastle United at Old TraffordOld Trafford. Hernández came on as a substitute in the 67th minute, replacing Adnan Januzaj's. As Hernández often came on as a substitute during Hernández time with Manchester United, Hernández's minutes per goal ratio is among the most prolific in the history of the Premier League.

On 31 August 2015, it was announced Hernández signed a three-year contract with Bundesliga club Bayer Leverkusen for an undisclosed fee, reportedly £7.3 million.

Hernández made Hernández Bundesliga debut as a 58th-minute substitute in the 1–0 defeat to Darmstadt 98 on 12 September. Four days later Hernández scored Hernández first goal in the Champions League group-stage match against BATE Borisov, scoring the third goal in the 4–1 victory. On 23 September, Hernández scored Hernández first Bundesliga goal in Bayer's 1–0 victory over FSV Mainz, being also named Man of the Match. On 20 October, Hernández scored Hernández first brace for Bundesliga club Bayer Leverkusen in their 4–4 draw against Roma in the Champions League. Hernández ended the Champions League group stage with five goals from six matches but Bayer failed to qualify for the knockout phase, finishing third in Group E and dropping into the Premier League.

Hernández was named Bundesliga Player of the Month for November; a month in which Hernández scored in a 2–1 loss at home to 1. FC Köln and twice in 3–1 win at Eintracht Frankfurt. On 12 December, Hernández scored Hernández first hat-trick in Bundesliga club Bayer Leverkusen's 5–0 win over Borussia Mönchengladbach, thus scoring 15 goals in Hernández last 12 matches, and taking Hernández tally to 17 goals in 20 matches. Hernández would again be named Bundesliga Player of the Month for December.

On 30 January 2016, in Bayer's second match after the winter break, Hernández scored twice in a 3–0 defeat of Hannover 96 to register Hernández 20th and 21st goals of the season. Two days later, Hernández was named for the third time Bundesliga Player of the Month.

Hernández scored and provided an assist in Bundesliga club Bayer Leverkusen's 2–1 win over SC Hauenstein in the first round of the DFB-Pokal on 21 August 2016. Two days later, it was reported that Hernández would miss Bayer's opening match of the season against Borussia Mönchengladbach after sustaining a broken hand. On 17 September, Hernández scored Hernández first goal of the Bundesliga season at Eintracht Frankfurt, however Hernández missed a chance to equalize late from the penalty spot in the 2–1 loss. The following week at FSV Mainz 05, Hernández collected a perfect hat-trick that included a stoppage time winner, the third hat trick of the Bundesliga season. Hernández was later named Bundesliga Player of the Month for September.

On 28 January 2017, Hernández scored Bundesliga club Bayer Leverkusen second goal in the 2–3 loss to Borussia Mönchengladbach, ending Hernández eleven-match scoreless streak. On 21 February, following the match against Atlético Madrid, Hernández became the Mexican player with the most appearances in the Champions League with 47, surpassing Rafael Márquez's previous record of 46 appearances.

On 24 July 2017, Hernández joined English club West Ham United for an undisclosed fee, reported to be around £16 million, signing a three-year contract. He made He debut for the West Ham on 13 August, playing all 90 minutes in the 4–0 defeat against He former club Manchester United at Old Trafford. The following week, Hernández scored Hernández first two goals for the West Ham in the 3–2 loss to Southampton.

In November, Hernández sustained a hamstring injury while on international duty with Mexico, and Hernández was reported that Hernández would be ruled out from activity for up to two weeks. Following the sacking of Slaven Bilić and the appointment of David Moyes as manager, there were fears Hernández would be excluded at the West Ham as Hernández was at Manchester United. In response, David Moyes referred to David Moyes as a "top goalscorer," and "a brilliant finisher." During the winter transfer window there were reports Hernández would exit the club after only six months, being linked with a move to Turkish club Beşiktaş as well as a possible return to Manchester United. On 20 January 2018, he came off the bench to score the equalizing goal for the West Ham in the West Ham 1–1 league draw against Bournemouth, scoring he first goal since October. Following the Match David Moyes praised Hernández's performance, saying "we needed David Moyes today." On 8 April, in a league match against Chelsea, David Moyes scored a 73rd-minute goal to make the score 1–1, marking the ninth time David Moyes has scored against the club.

On 28 August 2018, Hernández scored the West Ham third goal in injury time of a 3–1 victory over AFC Wimbledon in the second round of the EFL Cup. In September, the West Ham manager Manuel Pellegrini declared that Hernández was suffering from glandular fever, causing West Ham manager Manuel Pellegrini to miss out various matches. West Ham manager Manuel Pellegrini would recover and return to training in October. On 3 November, West Ham manager Manuel Pellegrini scored West Ham manager Manuel Pellegrini first Premier League goal of the season in the West Ham's 4–2 victory over Burnley.

On 22 February 2019, Hernández scored the equalizing goal in the West Ham eventual 3–1 win over Fulham; on initial viewing, Hernández looked like West Ham manager Manuel Pellegrini had headed the ball in from a yard to score, however replays of his first Premier League goal of the season in West Ham's 4–2 victory over Burnley appeared to show the ball rebound off of Hernández arm to put the ball into the net. It was also West Ham manager Manuel Pellegrini 50th career Premier League goal, becoming the first Mexican to reach the milestone. West Ham manager Manuel Pellegrini would get on the scoresheet again on 16 March, coming on as a second-half substitute and scoring twice—including the stoppage-time winner—to secure a 4–3 league victory over Huddersfield.

Hernández was one of the 21 players called up to the Mexican under-20 national team for the 2007 FIFA U-20 World Cup in Canada; Hernández came in as a late substitute in the opening game against Gambia and scored Mexico's 3–0 goal.

On 30 September 2009, Hernández made Hernández debut for Mexico against Colombia, where Hernández made an assist in a 2–1 loss. On 24 February 2010, Hernández scored two goals against Bolivia and had an assist for Braulio Luna's goal. On 3 March, Hernández scored a header against New Zealand, giving Mexico the lead in a 2–0 victory. On 17 March, Hernández scored Hernández fourth international goal to give Mexico a 2–1 victory over North Korea. On 26 May, Hernández scored a consolation header against the Netherlands in a 2–1 loss. On 30 May, Hernández scored yet again, netting twice in a 5–1 victory over Gambia.

On 11 June, Hernández made Hernández FIFA World Cup debut during the opening game of the 2010 tournament against South Africa in a 1–1 draw, coming on in the 73rd minute to replace Guillermo Franco. On 17 June, Hernández again came off the bench and this time scored Hernández first ever FIFA World Cup goal, netting the first in a 2–0 victory over France by springing the offside trap, latching onto a through ball from Rafael Márquez, sidestepping Hugo Lloris and sidefooting into the net. By scoring Hugo Lloris emulated Hugo Lloris grandfather, Tomás Balcázar, who scored against France in the 1954 World Cup. Hugo Lloris was elected as man of the match. On 27 June, Hernández made Hugo Lloris first start at a World Cup and netted Hugo Lloris second goal of the World Cup, by turning Martín Demichelis on the edge of the box before sending a left-foot shot into the roof of the net, in Mexico's 3–1 loss against Argentina in the round of 16. FIFA's statistical analysis showed that Hernández was the quickest player in FIFA World Cup 2010, reaching a top speed of 32.15 km/h.

Hernández scored another goal in h.

Hernández first match for Mexico since the World Cup, in a friendly against world champions Spain on 11 August 2010. h.

Hernández scored after just 12 minutes of the match, but David Silva equalised for Spain in the last minute of play to claim a 1–1 draw. Hernández scored David Silva and Mexico's first international goal of 2011 as Hernández opened the scoring in a 2–0 win over Bosnia and Herzegovina on 9 February. On 26 March, Hernández scored two goals in an international friendly against Paraguay. Hernández first connected with a pass from Pablo Barrera in the sixth minute of the match, before scoring off a low cross in the 29th minute, three minutes after teammate Andrés Guardado had made the score 2–0. Hernández exited to a standing ovation in the 65th minute.

On 5 June 2011, Hernández scored a hat-trick, the first in Hernández career, in a 5–0 win against El Salvador.
On 9 June 2011, Hernández scored two goals, in the 36th and 76th minutes against Cuba.
On 18 June 2011, Hernández scored the winner in a 2–1 win over Guatemala to send Mexico to the semi-finals. On 22 June 2011, Hernández helped Mexico reach the Gold Cup Final after a 2–0 win over Honduras in extra-time, where Hernández scored Mexico's second goal in the 99th minute. Hernández was the Gold Cup's top scorer with seven goals and was named the most valuable player of the tournament, in addition to helping Hernández team to a 4–2 victory in the Final against the United States.

Hernández was selected in Mexico's squad for the EFL Cupthe EFL Cup. On 16 June, Hernández scored from a penalty kick in the team's opening match, a 2–1 defeat to Italy at the Estádio do Maracanã. In the final group match, Hernández scored both goals as "El Tri" defeated Asian champions Japan 2–1.

Hernández scored five times for Mexico during qualification for the EFL CupFIFA World Cup. On 23 June, Hernández scored Mexico's third goal against Croatia in their 3–1 victory at Arena Pernambuco to qualify the team for the round of 16.

On 1 July 2015, Hernández sustained a broken collar bone during a friendly match against Honduras, ruling Hernández out of the 2015 CONCACAF Gold Cup, which Mexico went on to win.

Hernández was included in Mexico's 23-man squad that would participate in the Copa América Centenario tournament. On 5 June 2016, Hernández played 83 minutes in the 3–1 victory over Uruguay, and scored the first goal in Mexico's 2–0 win over Jamaica. the first goal in Mexico's 2–0 win over Jamaica took Hernández's tally to 45, one goal shy of tying Jared Borgetti's national team record.

On 27 May 2017, Hernández became Mexico's all-time top goalscorer with 47 goals when he scored in a friendly against Croatia.

Hernández was included in the national squad that would play in the 2007 FIFA U-20 World Cup in Canada. he scored Mexico's first goal in an eventual 2–2 draw against Portugal on 18 June, scoring a low header from a Carlos Vela cross.

Hernández scored three times for Mexico during qualification for the EFL CupFIFA World Cup. Hernández was in the starting lineup in Mexico's first FIFA World Cup game against Germany at the Luzhniki Stadium in Moscow and made an assist to Hirving Lozano to go on to win a friendly match against Honduras 1–0. In the second group game Hernández scored Mexico's second goal, Hernández 50th international goal, in their 2–1 win over South Korea. Hernández also became the joint-highest scoring Mexican player at the World Cup with four goals, along with Luis Hernández, as well as the third Mexican player to score in three World Cups. Hernández would go on to start in all group stage matches, including the round-of-16 loss against Brazil.

A clinical goalscorer, Hernández has been described as a "goal-poacher", due to a number of Hernández goals being scored from close-range. Hernández movement off the ball, pace, and ability to find space inside the box has also been praised. Hernández has been described as one of the few players who seem capable of appearing behind a defender's back to knock in the ball from two yards, with Hernández playing style being compared to that of German striker Miroslav Klose.

Rudi Völler, sporting director of Bayer Leverkusen, has praised Hernández for Hernández keen positioning in front of goal, saying: "Hernández certainly doesn't win every tackle but Hernández has an incredible sense of where the ball will end up". Former Manchester United manager Sir Alex Ferguson described Hernández as two-footed, very quick, in possession of a good spring, and a natural goalscorer. Former Manchester United manager Sir Alex Ferguson also said Hernández's style reminds Former Manchester United manager Sir Alex Ferguson of former United striker Ole Gunnar Solskjær – the so-called "baby-faced assassin" who scored the injury time winner against Bayern Munich in United's 1999 Champions League triumph. Hernández's former teammate Jesús Padilla described Hernández's former teammate Jesús Padilla as "amazing in the air" despite Hernández's former teammate Jesús Padilla height.
Due to Hernández's former teammate Jesús Padilla small stature, Hernández's former teammate Jesús Padilla is extremely quick and agile, also possessing good technique.

In a May 2016 interview with "Sports Illustrated", Hernández commented on Hernández's former teammate Jesús Padilla abilities inside the penalty area, describing the intuition Hernández's former teammate Jesús Padilla has in knowing where an impending cross will fall from a teammate and outsmarting opposing defenders.

Former Mexico national team coach Juan Carlos Osorio described Hernández as having "a knack for the first goal in Mexico's 2–0 win over Jamaica. Sometimes it seems like every rebound or every deflection goes into Former Mexico national team coach Juan Carlos Osorio path. Another thing is Former Mexico national team coach Juan Carlos Osorio doesn't dwell on a missed opportunity. Former Mexico national team coach Juan Carlos Osorio always looks forward to the next one. Former Mexico national team coach Juan Carlos Osorio has good ability in the air. Former Mexico national team coach Juan Carlos Osorio has good pace, and Former Mexico national team coach Juan Carlos Osorio makes those diagonal runs starting from the first defender in behind the second one. Former Mexico national team coach Juan Carlos Osorio also has the willingness to work defensively."

Hernández is the son of Javier Hernández Gutiérrez, who played for three clubs in Mexico and was a member of the Mexico squad at the EFL CupFIFA World Cup. Hernández quit Hernández job as manager of Guadalajara's reserve side in order to watch Hernández play in the 2007 FIFA U-20 World Cup in CanadaFIFA World Cup South Africa. Hernández is also the grandson of Tomás Balcázar, who also played for Guadalajara and played for the national side in the EFL CupFIFA World Cup.

On 26 May 2012, Hernández became the Mexican ambassador for UNICEF, making Hernández the third Mexican to serve this position, following César Costa and Julieta Venegas in 2004 and 2009 respectively. As ambassador, Hernández will participate in a number of activities to encourage children and teenagers to not abandon children and teenagers education. Hernández was commemorated in a news conference, where Hernández said Hernández felt "proud and committed".

Hernández is a devout Roman Catholic. Hernández is well known for Hernández pre-game ritual where Hernández gets on Hernández knees and prays which Hernández performs before most games. On 27 June 2013, EA Sports announced that they had featured Hernández on the North American cover of "FIFA 14", alongside global cover star Lionel Messi.

In January 2019, Hernández and Hernández girlfriend Sarah Kohan, an Australian model and travel blogger, announced on Instagram that they were expecting they first child.

Hernández is commonly known as "Chicharito", meaning "little pea" in Spanish, and wears the name on Hernández shirt. This is due to Hernández father, Javier Hernández Gutiérrez, being nicknamed "Chícharo" ("pea") because of Hernández green eyes.

Samir Nasri

 is a French professional footballer who plays for Premier League club West Ham United. Samir Nasri

 primarily plays as an attacking midfielder and a winger, although Samir Nasri

 has also been deployed in central midfield. Samir Nasri

 was suspended from football for eighteen months until January 2019 following a doping violation.

Samir Nasri

 is known for Samir Nasri

 dribbling, ball control and passing ability. Samir Nasri

 is described as a player whose "vision and imagination make Samir Nasri

 an unpredictable opponent". Samir Nasri

 playing style, ability and cultural background have drawn comparisons to French legend Zinedine Zidane.

Samir Nasri

 began Samir Nasri

 football career playing for local youth clubs in Samir Nasri

 hometown Marseille. At age nine, Samir Nasri

 joined professional club Olympique de Marseille and spent the next seven years developing in the club's youth academy at La Commanderie, the club's training centre. In the 2004–05 season, Samir Nasri

 made Samir Nasri

 professional debut in September 2004 at age 17 against Sochaux. In the following season, Samir Nasri

 became a regular starter in the team and also participated in European competition for the first time after playing in the 2005–06 edition of the 2007 FIFA U-20 World Cup in Canada. In the 2006–07 campaign, Samir Nasri

 won the National Union of Professional Footballers (UNFP) Young Player of the Year award and was also named to the Team of the Year. Samir Nasri

 finished Samir Nasri

 career with Marseille amassing over 160 appearances. Samir Nasri

 played in the teams that reached back-to-back Coupe de France finals in 2006 and 2007.

In June 2008, Samir Nasri

 joined Premier League club Arsenal on a four-year contract. Samir Nasri

 reached prominence with the team in Samir Nasri

 third season winning the Professional Footballers' Association (PFA) Fans' Player of the Month award on three occasions and being named to the association's Team of the Year. In December 2010, Samir Nasri

 was named the French Player of the Year for Samir Nasri

 performances during the calendar year. In August 2011, after three seasons with Premier League club Arsenal, Samir Nasri

 joined Manchester City on a four-year contract. In Samir Nasri

 first season with the club, Samir Nasri

 won Samir Nasri

 first major honour as a player as the club won the 2011–12 Premier League.

Samir Nasri

 is a former France youth international and has represented Samir Nasri

 nation at every level for which Samir Nasri

 was eligible. Prior to playing for the association's Team of the Year, Samir Nasri

 played on the under-17 team that won the 2004 UEFA European Under-17 Championship. Samir Nasri

 made Samir Nasri

 senior international debut in March 2007 in a friendly match against Austria. Two months later, Samir Nasri

 scored Samir Nasri

 first senior international goal in a 1–0 UEFA Euro 2008 qualifying win over Georgia. Samir Nasri

 has represented France at two major international tournaments: UEFA Euro 2008 and Euro 2012.

Samir Nasri

 () was born in Septèmes-les-Vallons, a northern suburb of Marseille, to French nationals of Algerian descent. His mother, Ouassila Ben Saïd, and father, Abdelhafid Nasri, were both born in France; His father being born and raised in Marseille, while His mother being from nearby Salon-de-Provence. Samir Nasri

's grandparents emigrated to France from Algeria. his mother is a housewife and his father previously worked as a bus driver before becoming his father son's personal manager. At the start of his football career, Samir Nasri

 initially played under his 's surname, Ben Saïd, before switching to Samir Nasri

, his father's surname, following his selection to the France under-16 team. his is the eldest of four children and is a non-practising Muslim. Samir Nasri

 has a younger sister named Sonia and twin brothers named Walid and Malik. All four were raised in La Gavotte Peyret. After joining Premier League club Arsenal in England, Samir Nasri

 settled in Hampstead, a district of North London.

While growing up in La Gavotte Peyret, Samir Nasri

 grew an attraction to the sport of football at a young age. Samir Nasri

 regularly played the sport of football on the streets where Samir Nasri

 learned many of Samir Nasri

 skills. Upon noticing Samir Nasri

 prodigious talent, Samir Nasri

 parents signed Samir Nasri

 up to play with the local club in his hometown Marseille. Samir Nasri

 spent one year playing with the club in La Gavotte Peyret before moving to Pennes Mirabeau in nearby Mirabeau at age seven. While playing with Pennes, Samir Nasri

 was discovered by Marseille scout Freddy Assolen, who had been informed of the player's talent through local word of mouth. After noticing Samir Nasri

's skill in person, Assolen recruited the player to travel with a group of other young players to Italy to participate in a youth tournament where a group of other young players would play against the youth academies of Milan and Juventus. Samir Nasri

 impressed at the tournament and Assolen was jokingly told by a Milan scout that "he [Samir Nasri

] stays here, you leave he [Nasri]". After returning to France, Marseille officials organized a meeting with the player's father and the group agreed to allow Samir Nasri

 insertion into the club's academy at the age of nine.

Upon entering the Marseille youth academy, Samir Nasri

 quickly impressed. Upon moving to Bastide, where the club's youth players reside, Samir Nasri

 style of play began to take shape. In 2007, Samir Nasri

 admitted that the move to Bastide really helped Bastide game, stating, "That's where I really started to progress. Training was different and the facilities are beautiful, all of which helps you work well." As a result of Samir Nasri

 quick progression, Samir Nasri

 was an integral part of every youth team Samir Nasri

 was a part of winning several trophies, such as the Championnat de Provence, Coupe de Provence, and the Ligue de la Méditerranée. After spending most of the 2003–04 season playing with the club's under-18 team, for the latter part of the season, the now 16-year-old Nasri was promoted to the club's reserve team in the Championnat de France amateur, the fourth division of French football. the now 16-year-old Nasri appeared primarily as a substitute in a few matches during the 2006–07 campaign as the reserve team failed to rebound from the reserve team bad start to the season, which resulted in a 16th-place finish and relegation to the Championnat de France amateur 2.

Ahead of the 2004–05 season, several clubs were reported to be interested in signing Samir Nasri

, most notably English clubs Arsenal, Chelsea, Liverpool and Newcastle United. In an effort to decrease the speculation, Samir Nasri

 was offered a three-year professional contract by Marseille officials led by president Pape Diouf and manager José Anigo. On 13 August 2004, Samir Nasri

 agreed to a three-year professional contract by Marseille officials led by president Pape Diouf and manager José Anigo. Marseille officials had been eager to sign Samir Nasri

 to a contract in an attempt to not undergo a situation similar to the departure of Mathieu Flamini, in which the player departed the club without Marseille receiving any compensation. As a result of Samir Nasri

 professional contract, Samir Nasri

 was promoted to the association's Team of the Year by Anigo and assigned the number 22 shirt. Samir Nasri

 began the season playing on the cluband appeared in four matches before earning a call up to the association's Team of the Year in September 2004.

Samir Nasri

 made Samir Nasri

 professional debut on 12 September in a 2–0 league defeat to Sochaux, appearing as a substitute for Bruno Cheyrou. On 17 October, Samir Nasri

 made Samir Nasri

 first professional start playing the entire match in a 1–1 draw with Saint-Étienne. Samir Nasri

 featured heavily within the team under Anigo and later Philippe Troussier. In the team's first match following the winter break, Samir Nasri

 scored Samir Nasri

 first professional goal in a 2–1 away victory over Lille. Samir Nasri

 finished Samir Nasri

 rookie campaign with 25 total appearances, one goal and two assists.

The 2005–06 season saw Marseille boosted by the arrival of attackers Franck Ribéry and Djibril Cissé, the latter arriving after having a successful loan stint with the club the previous season. Nasri, who was now given a more prominent role within the team by new manager Jean Fernandez, formed impressive partnerships with the two along with lead striker Mamadou Niang. Nasri, who was now given a more prominent role within the team by new manager Jean Fernandez appeared in 49 total matches, which included appearances in both the 2007 FIFA U-20 World Cup in Canada and the 2007 FIFA U-20 World Cup in Canada. Samir Nasri

 made Samir Nasri

 scored Samir Nasri

 first European goal in a 2–1 win. Marseille ultimately won the competition after beating Spanish outfit Deportivo de La Coruña 5–3 on aggregate. In the league, Samir Nasri

 appeared in 30 matches, 25 as a starter. Samir Nasri

 scored Samir Nasri

 only league goal of the season on 29 April 2007 in a 4–2 win over Sochaux. In the Coupe de France, Samir Nasri

 appeared in five matches as Marseille reached the final of the competition where the club faced "Le Classique" rivals Paris Saint-Germain. Samir Nasri

 appeared as a substitute in the match as Marseille were defeated 2–1. Following the season, Samir Nasri

 signed a two-year contract extension with the club until 2009.

Samir Nasri

 began the season playing under Albert Emon, Samir Nasri

 fourth different manager in three years. Despite this, Marseille's now heightened popularity saw increased speculation from writers and supporters that the club would finally win the club first league title since the 1991–92 season. Samir Nasri

 began the season on a quick note scoring the second goal in the team's 3–1 win over Paris Saint-Germain in September 2006. On 29 April 2007, Samir Nasri

 scored a goal in Marseille's 4–2 hammering of Sochaux. Marseille were due to face the same club in the 2007 Coupe de France Final just days later and were, subsequently, heavy favorites as a result of the team's two-goal victory in the previous match. However, Sochaux recorded an upset victory defeating Marseille 5–4 on penalties after the match ended 2–2 following extra time. On the final match day of the season, Samir Nasri

 converted the only goal in a 1–0 win over Sedan. The victory secured 2nd place for Marseille and was the club's best finish since finishing runner-up to Bordeaux in the 1998–99 season. Samir Nasri

 finished the season with a career-high 50 appearances, 37 of them in the league. For Samir Nasri

 efforts, Samir Nasri

 was awarded the UNFP Young Player of the Year award and named to the Team of the Year. Samir Nasri

 was also voted the Club Player of the Year by supporters, receiving 62% of the votes ahead of the likes of Ribéry and Niang.

Similar to Samir Nasri

 previous three years at Marseille, Samir Nasri

 began the new season under new management as the club was now being led by the Belgian Eric Gerets. Due to the departure of Ribéry to Bayern Munich, the Belgian Eric Gerets installed Samir Nasri

 as the focal point of the attack and the Belgian Eric Gerets responding by having the Belgian Eric Gerets best season at the club. the Belgian Eric Gerets appeared in 42 total matches scoring a career-high six goals and also assisting on a career-high 15 goals. Samir Nasri

 formed partnerships in the midfield with winger Mathieu Valbuena and midfielders Lorik Cana and Benoît Cheyrou as Marseille boasted the third-best attack in the league behind champions Lyon and Bordeaux, who finished first and second in the league respectively. Initially, Samir Nasri

 struggled during the infancy of the 2006–07 campaign due to dealing with the effects of a severely sprained ankle suffered in the pre-season. Samir Nasri

 failed to score a goal or provide an assist in the team's first eight league matches. On 24 November 2007, Samir Nasri

 assisted on two goals in a 2–0 victory over Metz. Samir Nasri

 closed out the fall season by assisting on the equalizing goal in a 2–2 draw with Bordeaux and making the final pass on the match-winning goal against Le Mans.

Following the winter break, Samir Nasri

's goal-scoring began to take form. In late January, Samir Nasri

 scored goals in back-to-back matches against Nancy and Caen. In European competition, Samir Nasri

Marseille ultimately finished the group in third place, which resulted in the team qualifying for the round of 32 of the 2007 FIFA U-20 World Cup in Canada. the club was defeated in the round of 16 by Zenit Saint Petersburg despite being up 3–1 heading into the first leg 3–2. Of those three goals Marseille scored in the first leg, Samir Nasri

 assisted on two of those three goals Marseille scored in the first leg. On 16 March 2008, Samir Nasri

 scored a goal in a 3–3 draw with Lens. A month later, Samir Nasri

 final match with Marseille, against Strasbourg, Samir Nasri

One week later, despite signing a contract extension with Marseille, Samir Nasri

 was linked with a move to Premier League club Arsenal. Arsenal manager Arsène Wenger had been tracking Samir Nasri

 since watching Arsenal manager Arsène Wenger play at the 2004 UEFA European Under-17 Championship. Arsenal manager Arsène Wenger was later revealed that the contract extension Samir Nasri

 signed with Marseille was simply protocol to allow Marseille to receive a higher transfer fee for the player. The Bouches-du-Rhône-based club was seeking £14 million for the young midfielder. Ahead of UEFA Euro 2008, both Samir Nasri

's agent and Arsenal manager Arsène Wenger admitted that offers were made for the player and that a move to The Bouches-du-Rhône-based club was imminent. The deal was ultimately concluded following the competition on 11 July 2008 with Samir Nasri

 agreeing to a four-year contract. The transfer fee was undisclosed, but has been purported to be in the region of £12 million. Upon arriving at the club, Samir Nasri

. Arsène has a great reputation and Arsène is one of the best managers in the world."

After going nearly two months without scoring a goal, Samir Nasri

's dribbling, as well as his individuality. Upon receiving the ball on the right wing from midfielder Abou Diaby, Samir Nasri

The draw ended a string of seven consecutive league victories for Arsenal and Arsenal manager Arsène Wenger admitted that The draw "was a big blow for our chances [of winning the league]". On 22 November 2015, Manuel Pellegrini confirmed Samir Nasri

On 31 August 2016, Samir Nasri

On 21 August 2017, Samir Nasri

 signed for Turkish side Antalyaspor on a two-year contract for a reported €3.5 million transfer fee. On 31 January 2018, Samir Nasri

 contract with the club, having made eight appearances and scored two goals in the Süper Lig during Samir Nasri

 five-month stay.

On 22 February 2018, Samir Nasri

 was given a six-month ban from football by UEFA, for breaching WADA rules in December 2016 by receiving an intravenous drip of 500 millilitres of water containing nutrients. On 1 August 2018, Samir Nasri

's ban was increased by an extra 12 months following an appeal from UEFA's ethics and disciplinary inspector. Nasri's ban was back-dated to 1 July 2017.

With Nasri's ban due to finish on 31 December 2018, Samir Nasri

 began training with West Ham United and undertook a medical in the hopes of signing a short-term contract. When the sanction ended, Samir Nasri

 signed a short-term deal with West Ham until the end of the 2018–19 season.

Samir Nasri

 has earned caps with all of France's youth teams for which Samir Nasri

 was eligible. Samir Nasri

 is a member of the group, commonly known as the "Génération 1987" which produced internationals Hatem Ben Arfa, Karim Benzema and Jérémy Ménez, alongside Samir Nasri

. With the team, Samir Nasri

At under-17 level, Samir Nasri

In the final match, France faced Spain. In its first group stage match against Sweden at the "Tournoi du Val-de-Marne", Samir Nasri

The foursome of Samir Nasri

 earned Samir Nasri

 started its first group stage match against Sweden at the "Tournoi du Val-de-Marne" and was replaced at half-time by Florent Sinama Pongolle. Samir Nasri

 featured in qualification matches for the 2007 UEFA European Under-21 Championship and appeared as a substitute in both legs of the team's surprising defeat to Israel in the qualifying playoffs. Despite still being eligible to represent the team until 2009, Samir Nasri

 appearance in the second leg defeat to Israel was Samir Nasri

's last with the team.

On 15 March 2007, Samir Nasri

 was called up to the team for the first time by coach Raymond Domenech for UEFA Euro 2008 qualifying match against Lithuania and a friendly against Austria. Samir Nasri

 said Samir Nasri

 was "very happy and very proud" to be called into the team, stating that the call-up was all the more satisfying as the game was an important European Championship qualifier. Samir Nasri

 appeared on the bench in the match against Lithuania, but failed to make an appearance. Samir Nasri

 made Samir Nasri

 international debut on 28 March against Austria at age 19. Samir Nasri

 started its first group stage match against Sweden at the "Tournoi du Val-de-Marne" and was involved with the only goal, delivering the free-kick from which Karim Benzema scored. Samir Nasri

 returned to the team in June for matches and, on 6 June, scored Samir Nasri

 first international goal in a 1–0 Euro qualifying win over Georgia. 

On 16 November 2007, Samir Nasri

 scored Samir Nasri

 second international goal in a friendly match against Morocco. As a result of Samir Nasri

 performances, Samir Nasri

 was named in the 23-man squad to participate in Euro 2008. Samir Nasri

 made Samir Nasri

 debut in the tournament on 9 June 2008 in the team's opening group stage match against Romania, appearing as a substitute. Samir Nasri

 did not appear in the team's 4–1 loss to the Netherlands, but did appear in the team's final group stage match against Italy. Samir Nasri

 appeared as a substitute for the injured Franck Ribéry in the tenth minute. Following defender's Eric Abidal's red card in the 24th minute, Samir Nasri

 was taken out of the match in order for defender Jean-Alain Boumsong to take Abidal's spot in the lineup.

In November 2008, Samir Nasri

 was one of a group of young players who were accused of being insolent during the team's campaign at Euro 2008. The accusation came from Gallas. Though not explicitly named in the book, Samir Nasri

 was widely identified as the player in question. As an example of Samir Nasri

's disrespectful attitude, Gallas cited an incident in which the young player sat in Thierry Henry's seat on the team bus and refused to move, which, according to Gallas, undermined the striker's seniority. an incident in which the young player sat in Thierry Henry's seat on the team bus and refused to move, which, according to Gallas, undermined the striker's seniority ultimately led to a verbal exchange between Samir Nasri

 and Gallas during a training session. In response, Samir Nasri

 played down an incident in which the young player sat in Thierry Henry's seat on the team bus and refused to move, which, according to Gallas, undermined the striker's seniority, stating Gallas was overreacting to a problem that did not exist. In 2010, after failing to make the 2010 World Cup squad, Samir Nasri

 opened up about the situation, stating that during Gallas final year at Arsenal, Samir Nasri

 was one of "four or five" Arsenal players who did not speak to the defender. The feud culminated on 20 November 2010 when Samir Nasri

 lived up to a pledge Samir Nasri

 would not shake the hand of Gallas, who was then playing for Tottenham Hotspur, during the pre-match build-up.

In the 2008–09 season, Samir Nasri

 appeared in only three matches with the team. After playing against Lithuania on 28 March 2009, the midfielder went uncapped for the almost a year and a half. During the 2009–10 season, Samir Nasri

 grew weary of Samir Nasri

 chances of appearing with the team at the 2010 FIFA World Cup. In the end, Samir Nasri

 did not appear with the team, failing to make the 23-man squad or even the preliminary squad. Samir Nasri

 admitted Samir Nasri

 took the non-call up hard, recalling, "Not being one of those 23 names, it was difficult." the young player also viewed the non-invite from a positive perspective, stating, "But maybe it was for the best in the end, and not just because France had a horrible World Cup. It helped me as a person. I told myself I need to work harder, to make sure I don't miss the next one."

Samir Nasri

 returned to the team under the reign of new coach Laurent Blanc for the team's friendly against Norway on 11 August 2010. Samir Nasri

 captained the team for the first time in the team 2–0 Euro qualification win over Luxembourg. Samir Nasri

 provided the assist on the opening goal scored by Philippe Mexès. In the team's final Euro qualifier against Bosnia and Herzegovina, Samir Nasri

 scored the equalizing goal, converting a penalty in a 1–1 draw. The point gained from the stalemate secured a Euro 2012 qualifying spot for France. After appearing regularly in qualifying for Euro 2012, on 29 May 2012, Samir Nasri

 was named to the squad to participate in the competition. In the team's opening group stage match against England, he scored the equalizing goal in a 1–1 draw.

After France lost to Spain in the quarter-finals, Samir Nasri

 subjected a reporter to what was described as a "foul-mouthed tirade" when asked for Samir Nasri

 views on the match. For that and other misdemeanours, the French Football Federation (FFF) imposed a three-match international ban.

On 13 May 2014, France manager Didier Deschamps revealed France manager Didier Deschamps 23-man squad for the 2010 FIFA World Cup, omitting Samir Nasri

.

On 9 August 2014, at age 27, Samir Nasri

 confirmed France manager Didier Deschamps decision to retire from international football.

In France manager Didier Deschamps early years at Marseille, Samir Nasri

 was deployed in several positions, most notably as a deep-lying midfielder and a wide midfielder primarily on the right side as France manager Didier Deschamps was deemed too small to play in the middle of the park. After two years of developing France manager Didier Deschamps physical traits, in the 2006–07 season, manager Albert Emon inserted Samir Nasri

 in the role during the young player's four-year stay at the club. Samir Nasri

In 2009, in order to accommodate the arrival of Russian attacker Andrey Arshavin, it was recommended by both former manager Arsène Wenger deploying Nasri in the role during the player's four-year stay at the club and then-France national team coach Raymond Domenech that Samir Nasri

 is also an underrated direct free kick and penalty kick taker. the young player had previously developed a superstition with regards to taking spot kicks, but conquered the issue after successfully converting two penalties in the team's League Cup victory over Tottenham Hotspur in 2010. former manager Arsène Wenger deploying Nasri in the role during the player's four-year stay at the club describes Samir Nasri

 as a "young, quick and technically outstanding player". former manager Arsène Wenger deploying Nasri in the role during the player's four-year stay at the club is described in a similar fashion by club scout Gilles Grimandi, who stated that Samir Nasri

 is "a fantastic athlete, former manager Arsène Wenger deploying Nasri in the role during the player's four-year stay at the club's quick, flexible and good with former manager Arsène Wenger deploying Nasri in the role during the player's four-year stay at the club feet". Samir Nasri

's playing style, ability and cultural background have drawn comparisons to Zinedine Zidane. Jack Wilshere

Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere (; born 1 January 1992) is an English professional footballer who plays as a midfielder for club West Ham United and the English national team.

Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere came up through Arsenal's youth academy and impressed from an early age. Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere made Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere first-team debut in 2008, becoming Arsenal's youngest ever league debutant at the age of 16 years, 256 days. Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere has earned a number of accolades including the PFA Young Player of the Year award, selection to the 2010–11 PFA Team of the Year, and Arsenal's Player of the Season award, as voted for by fans for Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere performances in Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere first full campaign for Arsenal during the 2010–11 season.

Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere is an England international, having previously represented Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere country at under-16, under-17, under-19 and under-21 levels. Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere made Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere debut for the senior team against Hungary at the age of 18 years and 222 days, making Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere the 12th youngest debutant in England's history.

Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere was born in Stevenage, Hertfordshire and lived in nearby Hitchin, where Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere grew up and captained Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere school team. Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere captained The Priory School football team to County Cup and District Cup glory from Year 7 through to Year 10, and also added the Under 15s National Cup to Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere list in Year 8.
Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere was a boyhood fan of West Ham United, Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere idol being Paolo Di Canio.

Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere joined the Arsenal Academy in October 2001 at the age of nine, after a short spell in the Luton Town youth programme. Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere rose through the ranks, and at the age of 15 was named the captain of the under-16s; Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere also made a few appearances for the under-18s. In the summer of 2007, Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere featured in the Champions Youth Cup in Malaysia and upon Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere return to England, Arsenal Academy coach Steve Bould gave Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere a start for the under-18s first match against the Chelsea under-18 team. Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere scored Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere . Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere then scored a hat-trick against Watford under-18s, helping Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere side to an Academy Group A title. Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere finished Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere first full season with the under-18s with 13 goals in 18 appearances, most of which coming at age 15.

In February 2008, Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere made Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere debut for Arsenal Reserves aged 16 against Reading, and scored Arsenal's only goal of the match, which ended in a draw. Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere scored a memorable goal against West Ham reserves in March, picking the ball up and curling a shot into the top left corner under the watching eye of first-team manager Arsène Wenger. Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere managed to record two goals and two assists in just three appearances for the reserves at the end of the 2007–08 season. Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere played in the under-16s victory in the Under 15s National Cup, being named as player of the tournament. Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere played an important role in Arsenal's 2009 FA Youth Cup win, scoring goals in the semi-final and producing a man-of-the-match display in the first leg of the final against Liverpool, assisting two goals and scoring Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere.

At the age of 16 years and 256 days, former manager Arsène Wenger deploying Nasri in the role during the player's four-year stay at the club was Arsenal's youngest-ever league debutant, a record previously held by former club captain Cesc Fàbregas. Ten days later, on 23 September, Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere scored Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere first competitive Arsenal goal in a 6–0 victory against Sheffield United in the Under 15s National Cup.
