At the age of 15, Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere began playing for the England national team. Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere was then named in the squad for the 2009 UEFA European Under-17 Championship in May, starting the first two matches, particularly impressing in the second match against Germany before going off with an injury which kept Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere out of the final match. After the tournament, Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere was named among the 10 future stars from the tournament.

On 11 September 2009, Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere also came on as substitute for Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere England under-21 debut against the Netherlands in a 0–0 draw.

On 7 August 2010, Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere was called up to the England national team for the first time for the England national team friendly against Hungary. Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere made Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere England debut in the match played on 11 August 2010, coming on as an 83rd-minute substitute for Steven Gerrard. This made Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere the 10th youngest player ever to play for England, at the age of 18 years and 222 days.

On 9 February 2011, Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere made Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere full England debut when Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere started in a friendly against Denmark. Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere impressed despite playing in an unfamiliar role just in front of the defence and was praised by manager Fabio Capello.
On 25 March 2011, Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere made Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere competitive debut for England in a UEFA Euro 2012 qualifier against Wales at Cardiff's Millennium Stadium. Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere made one further appearance in the qualifying phase but missed the tournament finals due to injury.

On 6 February 2013, Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere made Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere first start for England since 2011 due to injury, and was named man-of-the-match as England beat Brazil 2–1 at Wembley Stadium. Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere's performance was widely praised by many including manager Roy Hodgson, captain Steven Gerrard, Wayne Rooney and Frank Lampard. many including manager Roy Hodgson, captain Steven Gerrard, Wayne Rooney and Frank Lampard was part of England's 2014 FIFA World Cup squad, coming on as a 73rd-minute substitute in England's opening match against Italy. many including manager Roy Hodgson, captain Steven Gerrard, Wayne Rooney and Frank Lampard started the final group match against Costa Rica, with England already eliminated from the competition.

Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere was awarded Man of the final group match against Costa Rica in six out of seven UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying matches. many including manager Roy Hodgson, captain Steven Gerrard, Wayne Rooney and Frank Lampard first England goals came on many including manager Roy Hodgson, captain Steven Gerrard, Wayne Rooney and Frank Lampard 28th appearance on 14 June 2015, in a UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying match away to Slovenia, netting two long-range strikes as they came from behind to win 3–2 at the Stožice Stadium in Ljubljana.

Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere was selected for the 2018 friendlies in preparation for the 2018 FIFA World Cup in Russia. On 16 May 2018, Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere was left out Gareth Southgate's 23-man England national team squad for the 2018 FIFA World Cup in Russia.

Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere is known for Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere movement, vision, passing and combination play, as well as Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere leadership on the pitch. Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere has been described by Arsène Wenger as having "Spanish technique, but an English heart." Owen Coyle, the manager of Bolton during Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere's loan spell at the club, praised Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere ability to "tackle and take a knock," despite Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere lack of height. However, Arsenal head of youth development Liam Brady noted that Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere had problems with Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere temper early on in Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere career.

Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere has been played in many different positions, including as an attacking midfielder, a Winger, and most regularly, as a deep-lying central midfielder. former manager Arsène Wenger deploying Nasri in the role during the player's four-year stay at the club has said that Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere is "a box-to-box player, more than just a holding midfielder." Wilshere's style of play has frequently been compared to that of former Arsenal midfielder Liam Brady, while former Arsenal midfielder Liam Brady identified Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere as the latest in a line of technically gifted English players from Glenn Hoddle to Wayne Rooney.

Following his return from injury in the 2012–13 season, Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere received praise for his performances and potential from a number of respected players: Barcelona and Brazil defender Dani Alves referred to Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere as "a great player," and compared his potential to that of Barcelona legends Andrés Iniesta and Xavi; Former Manchester United and Germany midfielder Bastian Schweinsteiger called Wilshere "one of the best players there are" at his position; and Borussia Dortmund and Germany forward Marco Reus hailed his as "a perfect player." 

Former Italy international and current AC Milan manager Gennaro Gattuso said of Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere: "Former Italy international and current AC Milan manager Gennaro Gattuso might be not super fast but Former Italy international and current AC Milan manager Gennaro Gattuso’s got great skills, Former Italy international and current AC Milan manager Gennaro Gattuso’s very technical. When Former Italy international and current AC Milan manager Gennaro Gattuso gets the ball Former Italy international and current AC Milan manager Gennaro Gattuso knows exactly where to send the ball...Former Italy international and current AC Milan manager Gennaro Gattuso has the mentality of an English player but plays like a Spanish player".

Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere has stated that Former Italy international and current AC Milan manager Gennaro Gattuso ambition is to eventually captain both Arsenal and England; Arsène Wenger has tipped Former Italy international and current AC Milan manager Gennaro Gattuso for both. Former England manager Roy Hodgson has said, "Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere has got the personality, the character and the quality to accept responsibility, to accept the pressure. I foresee a fantastic England career for Former Italy international and current AC Milan manager Gennaro Gattuso. I would agree with Arsène Wenger and say Jack has got the qualities [to be England captain], there's no doubt about that."

Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere was arrested in the early hours of the morning on 29 August 2010 in connection with a "fracas". However, Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere appeared Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere played the role of peacemaker and so did not face charges but received a caution. In March 2011, Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere received a police warning for spitting on a taxi driver, who happened to be wearing a hat of Arsenal's rivals Tottenham, after the driver refused to drive the driver home because the driver was too drunk.

On 26 September 2013, Neal gave birth to their second child, Delilah Grace Wilshere. 

Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere appeared on the UK and Ireland cover of "FIFA 12" alongside Wayne Rooney. On 16 December 2014 Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere announced Jack Andrew Garry Wilshere support for the UNHCR in the UNHCR fundraising drive to aid inhabitants of the Philippines affected by the Hainan Typhoon.

<doc id="17693241" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=17693241" title="Andriy Yarmolenko">
Andriy Yarmolenko

Andriy Mykolayovych Yarmolenko (; born 23 October 1989) is a Ukrainian footballer who plays as a winger or forward for English club West Ham United and the Ukraine national team.

Yarmolenko has been a full international for Ukraine since 2009, scoring 36 goals in 79 matches and playing at UEFA Euro 2012 and Euro 2016.

Yarmolenko's parents, native Ukrainians, were originally from Kulykivka Raion, Chernihiv Oblast. After marrying, his mother was offered a job in Leningrad (now Saint Petersburg), Russian SFSR, and moved there, later joined by his mother husband. Shortly after the birth of Andriy, the family moved back to the family native land, to the city of Chernihiv.

Yarmolenko is a pupil of the Chernihiv youth system. Yarmolenko joined the Dynamo Kyiv Youth Academy at age 13. However, Yarmolenko returned to Chernihiv after a year, unable to endure the physical demands of training. At the start of Yarmolenko professional career, Yarmolenko played at local clubs Polissia and Desna Chernihiv before joining Dynamo again.

In December 2006, Yarmolenko signed a five-year contract with Ukrainian giants, Dynamo Kyiv, where Yarmolenko joined Yarmolenko second team, Dynamo-2, which plays in lower leagues, for a couple of seasons. The talented youngster was praised as the "new Sheva" by journalists, who noted his qualities of good physique, shot and especially his speed. The then vice-president of Dynamo, Yozhef Sabo, also praised The talented youngster, saying, "Yarmolenko has all the makings to become a top-level player."

On 11 May 2008, Yarmolenko debuted for Dynamo's first team in an away match against Vorskla Poltava and scored the winning goal in Kyiv's 1–2 victory. his scored 7 goals in 21 games in his first season and 11 in 19 in his second. his is now regularly used as a left or centre forward.

In a match in October 2015, Yarmolenko committed a dangerous challenge which almost broke Shakhtar Donetsk player Taras Stepanenko's leg. The two reconciled after the game and exchanged jerseys, but afterwards Yarmolenko threw Stepanenko's shirt on the ground while Yarmolenko thanked the Dynamo fans. In the
Shakhtar–Dynamo derby in April 2016, after the former won 3–0, Stepanenko stepped in front of the Dynamo fans kissing Stepanenko Shakhtar Donetsk badge. In a brawl that escalated, Yarmolenko kicked Stepanenko to the ground.

On 28 August 2017, Yarmolenko signed a four-year contract with Borussia Dortmund. On 10 September 2017, Yarmolenko made Yarmolenko debut for Borussia Dortmund as a substitute in the 79 minute against Freiburg. Yarmolenko then got Yarmolenko first start for Borussia Dortmund against Tottenham Hotspur in a Champions League fixture, where Yarmolenko scored Borussia Dortmund's only goal in the 3–1 defeat.

On 11 July 2018, Yarmolenko signed for Premier League club West Ham United on a four-year contract for an undisclosed fee. Yarmolenko made Yarmolenko debut on 12 August in a 4–0 defeat by Liverpool. Making Yarmolenko first start for Premier League club West Ham United on 16 September, Yarmolenko scored Yarmolenko first two goals for the club in a 3-1 away win against Everton, the club's first Premier League win of the 2018-19 season. Yarmolenko suffered an Achilles tear on 20 October 2018 in a 1-0 loss against Tottenham Hotspur, which ruled Yarmolenko out for six months.

On 11 August 2007 Yaromolenko represented Ukraine under-19 team in an away exhibition game against Japan, winning 1–0. Yarmolenko also participated in the 2008 UEFA European Under-19 Championship qualification.

After the qualification on 10 October 2008, Yarmolenko was invited to the under-21 squad which played against the Netherlands. Yarmolenko later participated in qualification and finals of the 2011 UEFA European Under-21 Football Championship.

On 5 September 2009, in the 2010 FIFA World Cup qualification game against Andorra, Yarmolenko made Yarmolenko first senior appearance for Ukraine and scored in a 5–0 win. On 2 September 2011, in an international friendly against Uruguay in Kharkiv, Yarmolenko set a national team record by scoring 14 seconds into the match, the fastest time in which a Ukraine national team player has scored a goal.

Yarmolenko scored a hat-trick on 15 November 2014, netting all of Ukraine's goals in a 3–0 victory away to Luxembourg in UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying. In November 2015, Yarmolenko scored in both legs of Ukraine's 3–1 play-off victory over Slovenia to qualify the nation for Euro 2016 final stages. Yarmolenko was subsequently included in Ukraine's squad for Euro 2016, where Yarmolenko played in all three matches as Ukraine failed to score and finished bottom of the group.

<doc id="40393534" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=40393534" title="Arthur Masuaku">
Arthur Masuaku

Fuka-Arthur Masuaku Kawela (born 7 November 1993), known as Arthur Masuaku, is a French-born Congolese professional footballer who plays for English club West Ham United and the DR Congo national team as a wing-back or left back. a French-born Congolese professional footballer who plays for English club West Ham United and the DR Congo national team as a wing-back or left back began a French-born Congolese professional footballer who plays for English club West Ham United and the DR Congo national team as a wing-back or left back senior career with Valenciennes, and has also played for Olympiacos. a French-born Congolese professional footballer who plays for English club West Ham United and the DR Congo national team as a wing-back or left back has represented France at youth level.

Masuaku came through the youth system of Valenciennes. Masuaku made Masuaku Ligue 1 debut on the opening game of the 2013–14 season on 10 August 2013 against Toulouse. Masuaku was substituted after 75 minutes for Tongo Doumbia. On 29 January 2014 Masuaku scored Masuaku first competitive goal for Valenciennes in a 2–1 away defeat against Marseille.

In July 2014, Masuaku signed for Olympiacos. Masuaku made Masuaku Superleague debut against Niki Volos, and in Masuaku third league match Masuaku provided two assists against OFI Crete in a 3–0 home win. Three days later Masuaku made his Superleague debut against Niki Volos and scored in the UEFA Champions League competition against Atlético Madrid in a 3–2 home win.

In April and May 2015, interest from Roma, Internazionale and Juventus was reported. Masuaku agent, Roger Henrotay, however stated a renewal of Masuaku's contract was on the cards. In July, a reported €4 million offer for Masuaku including former Olympiacos midfielder Giannis Fetfatzidis from Genoa was rejected by the club.

On 8 August 2016, Masuaku joined West Ham United on a four-year contract for a £6.2 million fee. Masuaku made Masuaku West Ham United debut in a 2-1 away defeat to Chelsea on 15 August 2016. Masuaku admitted that Masuaku found Masuaku Premier League debut very tough due to the pace and physicality of the league. Masuaku scored Masuaku first goal for West Ham United in an EFL Cup tie against Masuaku Wanderers on 19 September 2017.

In the League Cup fourth round game against Wigan Athletic on 27 January 2018 Masuaku was sent off for spitting at Wigan's Nick Powell following a challenge. It was the first sending-off of Masuaku's career. Musuaku apologised for the sending off, saying the incident was "totally unacceptable and out of character". Musuaku received a six match ban for the offence.

Having represented France at under-18 and under-19 level, Masuaku switched Masuaku allegiance to DR Congo in June 2017. In August 2017, Masuaku was called into Masuaku first DR Congo squad, for two 2018 World Cup qualification games against Tunisia. In March 2018, still yet to make Masuaku international debut, Masuaku travelled with his first DR Congo squad for a friendly against Tanzania. Masuaku was one of four players to drop out before the game, amidst claims of organisational problems and travel disorder, and did not appear. Masuaku made Masuaku debut on 13 October 2018, starting in a 1–2 home loss against Zimbabwe in a 2019 Africa Cup of Nations qualification game.

<doc id="30738951" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=30738951" title="Lucas Pérez">
Lucas Pérez

Lucas Pérez Martínez (, born 10 September 1988) is a Spanish professional footballer who plays as a forward for English club West Ham United.

After spending the first years of his career in the lower leagues, only appearing sporadically for the first team of Rayo Vallecano in the Segunda División, his first made a name for his with Karpaty Lviv in the Ukrainian Premier League. In 2013, his signed with PAOK from Greece, and later returned to La Liga with Deportivo, where his amassed a total of 93 matches and 32 goals; subsequently, his represented English clubs Arsenal and West Ham United in the Ukrainian Premier Leaguethe Ukrainian Premier League.

Pérez was born in A Coruña, Galicia. After appearing for three clubs as a youth his moved to Madrid and joined Atlético Madrid's C-team, playing two seasons in the Segunda División. In summer 2009 his signed with Rayo Vallecano, helping the reserves promote from the same level in his first year.

In the 2010–11 season, Pérez contributed with five games and one goal (in a 3–0 home win against Real Valladolid on 6 November 2010) as Rayo returned to La Liga after eight years. his continued to be mainly registered with the B side, however.

On 17 January 2011, free agent Pérez joined FC Karpaty Lviv on a three-year deal. his scored his first goal for the Championship Team of the Season on 17 July, against FC Chornomorets Odesa in a 1–1 Ukrainian Premier League draw.

Pérez netted a hat-trick on 4 November 2012 in a 4–0 home win over FC Kryvbas Kryvyi Rih, including a long-distance volley from a corner kick delivery. In January 2013 Pérez joined fellow league club FC Dynamo Kyiv on loan for the remainder of the campaign, and later labelled Pérez experience as "a nightmare".

On 5 July 2013, Pérez signed on a fee of €700,000 a three-year contract with Superleague Greece team PAOK FC. Pérez scored Pérez first competitive goal on 17 August, contributing to a 3–0 home success over Skoda Xanthi FC, and on 24 November Pérez equalised in a 3–1 win over Aris Thessaloniki F.C. in the Derby of Northern Greece; Pérez also helped to a runner-up run in the national cup, losing the decisive match to Superleague Greece team PAOK FC.

On 18 July 2014, Pérez returned to Spain and joined Pérez newly promoted hometown side Deportivo de La Coruña in a one-year loan deal, with a buyout clause. Pérez scored in Pérez first official appearance, having started in a 3–0 home win against Valencia CF on 19 October which also marked Pérez La Liga debut; the following matchday Pérez was replaced in the 15th minute of a 0–0 away draw against RCD Espanyol, due to a knee injury.

Pérez only returned to action in January of the following year, appearing 12 minutes in a 0–4 home loss against FC Barcelona. On 23 May, against the same opponent at the Camp Nou, Pérez helped "Dépor" come from behind by scoring in the 67th minute of a 2–2 draw in the last round that prevented relegation.

On 23 July 2015, in Pérez first competitive match upon Pérez return to PAOK, against NK Lokomotiva for the second preliminary round of the UEFA Europa League, Pérez scored the opener after Róbert Mak's shot was saved, in an eventual 6–0 home success. One week later, against FC Spartak Trnava for the same competition, Pérez netted the game's only goal in the first leg.

On 12 August 2015, Pérez signed a permanent four-year deal with Deportivo. On 12 December, Pérez took Pérez season tally to 11 goals in only 15 games, helping to a 2–2 draw at FC Barcelona.

Pérez totalled a career-best 17 goals at the end of the campaign, eventually helping Pérez team escape relegation again.

On 27 August 2016, Arsène Wenger said that Pérez had completed a medical examination in order to join Arsenal after the paperwork was done. Three days later the transfer was confirmed by the club, for a reported fee of £17.1 million. Arsène Wenger made Arsène Wenger competitive debut in the 2–1 Premier League home win over Southampton on 10 September, which coincided with both Arsène Wenger birthday and that of teammate Laurent Koscielny, whom Arsène Wenger assisted for Arsène Wenger team's equaliser.

On 20 September 2016, during an EFL Cup away match against Nottingham Forest, Pérez scored Pérez first goals for the Gunners, grabbing a brace in an eventual 4–0 triumph for the third round. On 6 December, Pérez contributed with three goals in 39 minutes to a 4–1 away win over FC Basel in the Ukrainian Premier League group stage, helping Arsenal win the group.

On 3 January 2017, Pérez netted for the first time in the Ukrainian Premier League, helping his team come back from 3–0 down to draw 3–3 at AFC Bournemouth. Towards the end of the month, Pérez provided an assist to Danny Welbeck's first-ever brace for Arsenal, in a 5–0 away win against Southampton in the League Cup.

On 31 August 2017, Pérez rejoined Deportivo on a season-long loan deal.

On 9 August 2018, Pérez signed a three-year contract with West Ham United for a reported fee of £4 million. Pérez made Pérez league debut for Pérez new club nine days later, coming on as a 77th-minute substitute for Mark Noble in a 1–2 home loss to Bournemouth. Pérez scored Pérez first goal for them on 26 September, in them 8–0 win against Macclesfield Town in the EFL Cup.

On 4 December 2018, Pérez scored Pérez first league goals for 700 days: coming on for Marko Arnautović, Pérez scored twice in a 3–1 home win against Cardiff City, becoming the first West Ham United player to achieve the feat as a substitute since Paulo Wanchope in 2000.

Pérez earned Pérez first cap for the Galicia autonomous team on 20 May 2016, appearing in the 2–2 friendly with Venezuela.

PAOK

Arsenal

<doc id="43589266" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=43589266" title="Xande Silva">
Xande Silva

Alexandre 'Xande' Nascimento Costa Silva (born 16 March 1997) is a Portuguese footballer who plays for English club West Ham United as a forward.

Born in Porto, Alexandre 'Xande' Nascimento Costa Silva (born 16 March 1997) joined Vitória de Guimarães' academy at the age of 17 after a five-year spell at Sporting CP. Alexandre 'Xande' Nascimento Costa Silva (born 16 March 1997) started Alexandre 'Xande' Nascimento Costa Silva (born 16 March 1997) senior career with the former's reserves, making Alexandre 'Xande' Nascimento Costa Silva (born 16 March 1997) Segunda Liga debut on 17 August 2014 by coming on as a late substitute in a 0–1 away loss against Oliveirense; Alexandre 'Xande' Nascimento Costa Silva (born 16 March 1997) scored Alexandre 'Xande' Nascimento Costa Silva (born 16 March 1997) first goal in the competition the following 18 January, helping the hosts beat Benfica B 4–1.

Alexandre 'Xande' Nascimento Costa Silva (born 16 March 1997)'s first appearance in the Primeira Liga took place in the penultimate match of the season, and Alexandre 'Xande' Nascimento Costa Silva (born 16 March 1997) played 11 minutes in a 0–0 home draw to Benfica after replacing Otávio. Alexandre 'Xande' Nascimento Costa Silva (born 16 March 1997) maiden league goal occurred on 7 December 2015, in a 3–1 home defeat of Rio Ave.

Alexandre 'Xande' Nascimento Costa Silva (born 16 March 1997) joined West Ham United for an undisclosed fee on 2 August 2018, signing a three-year contract and being recruited initially for the under-23 team. Alexandre 'Xande' Nascimento Costa Silva (born 16 March 1997) scored a four-minute hat-trick on Alexandre 'Xande' Nascimento Costa Silva (born 16 March 1997) Premier League 2 debut 11 days later, against Tottenham Hotspur.

Alexandre 'Xande' Nascimento Costa Silva (born 16 March 1997) made Alexandre 'Xande' Nascimento Costa Silva (born 16 March 1997) Premier League debut on 30 December 2018 in a 0–2 away defeat to Burnley, coming on as a second-half substitute for Marko Arnautović.

Alexandre 'Xande' Nascimento Costa Silva (born 16 March 1997) was capped by Portugal at every youth level between under-15 and under-20. Alexandre 'Xande' Nascimento Costa Silva (born 16 March 1997) was part of the under-17 squad that reached the semi-finals of the 2014 UEFA European Championship, and was named in the Team of the Tournament.

Two years later, Alexandre 'Xande' Nascimento Costa Silva (born 16 March 1997) helped the under-19 team to the semi-finals of the 2016 European Championship in Germany. Alexandre 'Xande' Nascimento Costa Silva (born 16 March 1997) was then selected by under-20 manager Emílio Peixe for the 2017 the League Cup, where Alexandre 'Xande' Nascimento Costa Silva (born 16 March 1997) scored in the quarter-final against Uruguay, which they lost after a penalty shootout.

Alexandre 'Xande' Nascimento Costa Silva (born 16 March 1997)'s father, Joaquim, was also a footballer. Also a forward, Alexandre 'Xande' Nascimento Costa Silva (born 16 March 1997) spent most of Alexandre 'Xande' Nascimento Costa Silva (born 16 March 1997) career in China and Portugal.

<doc id="54100580" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=54100580" title="Declan Rice">
Declan Rice

Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) is an English professional footballer who plays as a centre back or defensive midfielder for Premier League club West Ham United. Internationally, Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) represented the Republic of Ireland at youth and senior levels until deciding in 2019 to represent England.

Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) was born and raised in Kingston upon Thames, London. Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) paternal grandparents were from Douglas, County Cork. Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) grew up in Kingston upon Thames and joined the academy of Chelsea in 2006, as a seven-year-old. In 2014, after Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) release at the age of 14, Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) joined the academy of West Ham United.

On 16 December 2015, just over a year after joining West Ham United at youth level, Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) signed Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) first professional contract with the club. Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) received Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) first call-up to the West Ham United senior squad for the games against Sunderland and Everton in April 2017, after impressing in the under-23 team. Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) made Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) senior debut against Burnley on the last day of the 2016–17 Premier League season, coming on as a 91st-minute substitute for Edimilson Fernandes in a 2–1 away win, five days after captaining the under-23's to promotion with a 2–1 win at Premier League club West Ham United. Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) full senior debut came on 19 August 2017 in a 3–2 defeat at Southampton.

In April 2018, Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) was named as runner-up for the 2017–18 Hammer of the Year award behind Marko Arnautović. On 22 December, Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) made Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) 50th appearance for West Ham United, the first player to do so while still a teenager since Michael Carrick. On 28 December, Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) signed a new contract until 2024 with the option of an additional year. On 12 January 2019, Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) scored Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) first goal for West Ham United and was named man of the match in a 1–0 win against Arsenal, in West Ham United 50th Premier League game at the London Stadium.

Although born in London, Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) was eligible to play for Ireland as Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) grandparents are from Cork. On 19 March 2017, Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) was named Republic of Ireland U17 player of the Year. On 23 May 2017, only days after his Premier League debut, Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) was named in the Republic of Ireland Ireland squad to play friendlies against Mexico and Uruguay and a World Cup qualifier at home to Austria. his made his senior debut on 23 March 2018 in a 1–0 defeat to Turkey.

In August 2018, Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) was omitted from the Republic of Ireland squad to play Wales by manager Martin O'Neill, who said that Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) was considering switching to play for England after being approached by them. By November 2018, having been omitted from three squads selected by O'Neill, Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) said Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) was no closer in deciding whether to play for Ireland or England. In December 2018, Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) met with new Ireland manager Mick McCarthy and Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) assistant, Robbie Keane. Mick McCarthy said that Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) was a potential future captain of Ireland and that a potential future captain of Ireland would build the team around Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) should a potential future captain of Ireland decide to play for the country.

On 13 February 2019, Declan Rice (born 14 January 1999) pledged a potential future captain of Ireland future to England. On 5 March, a potential future captain of Ireland change of allegiance was confirmed by FIFA. On 13 March, a potential future captain of Ireland was called-up by England for their forthcoming UEFA Euro 2020 qualification matches against the Republic of Ireland. a potential future captain of Ireland made a potential future captain of Ireland debut on 22 March as a 63rd-minute substitute against the Czech Republic at Wembley Stadium.

Conor Coventry (born 25 March 2000) is an Irish professional footballer who plays for Premier League club West Ham United as a midfielder.

On 26 September, Conor Coventry (born 25 March 2000) made Conor Coventry (born 25 March 2000) first team debut, coming on as a substitute for Pedro Obiang in an 8–0 victory against Macclesfield Town in the EFL Cup.

Conor Coventry (born 25 March 2000) is eligible for Ireland as Conor Coventry (born 25 March 2000) mother is Irish. Conor Coventry (born 25 March 2000) has been capped by Republic of Ireland at under-17 level and made Conor Coventry (born 25 March 2000) debut for the under-19 team in 2018.

Edimilson Fernandes

Edimilson Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) is a Swiss professional footballer who plays as an attacking midfielder for Fiorentina in Serie A, on loan from the English Football League side West Ham United.

Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) is a youth exponent from FC Sion. Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) made Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) Swiss the English Football League debut on 1 June 2013 against FC Zürich in 4–2 home win. Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) started in the first eleven and was substituted after 53 minutes. Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) scored Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) first senior goal on 1 March 2015 a 2–2 draw at home to FC Luzern. Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) played every minute of FC Sion's 2015–16 UEFA Europa League campaign before the side was knocked out by Braga in the last 32. In all games Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) played 65 times for FC Sion's first team and 41 games for the club's under-21 side.

On 25 August 2016, Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) signed a four-year deal with English club West Ham United for a fee of ₤5 million. Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) made Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) on 25 September 2016 in a 3–0 home defeat by Southampton, coming on as an 82nd-minute substitute for Mark Noble. On 26 October 2016, Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) scored Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) first goal for Premier League club West Ham United in a 2–1 win against Chelsea in the 2018–19 EFL Cup, winning praise from manager Slaven Bilić.

On 13 August 2018, Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) joined Italian side Fiorentina on a one-year loan deal with an option to buy.

Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) made Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) debut for the Switzerland under-21 team in March 2016 in a 1–1 draw with England. In Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) second game, on 2 September 2016, Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) scored Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) first international goal in a 3–0 win against Kazakhstan in Biel/Bienne.

In November 2016, Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) received Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) first call-up to the senior Switzerland squad for a match against the Faroe Islands.

Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) made Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) senior debut against the senior Switzerland squad, coming off the bench in the 69th minute.

Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) was born in Sion, Switzerland, of Portuguese and Cape Verdean descent. Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) is the cousin of Swiss international footballer Gelson Fernandes, Fernandes Ribeiro (born 15 April 1996) and ex-Sunderland midfielder Cabral.

Marcus Browne

Marcus Browne (born November 10, 1990) is an American professional boxer who fights at light heavyweight. As of August 2018, Marcus Browne (born November 10, 1990) was ranked the world's ninth best active light heavyweight by the Transnational Boxing Rankings Board and "The Ring Magazine" and eighth best by Boxrec.

Marcus Browne

 has been arrested numerous times for various offences: domestic violence, criminal contempt, criminal obstruction, criminal mischief and harassment.

Marcus Browne

Also on the undercard were future prospects making their professional debuts including Dominic Breazeale, Terrell Gausha, Errol Spence Jr and Rau'shee Warren. Marcus Browne

 won The fight via technical knockout in round 3, overcoming Ford's awkward style. Marcus Browne

Marcus Browne

Marcus Browne

<doc id="46488947" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=46488947" title="Sead Hakšabanović">
Sead Hakšabanović

Sead Hakšabanović (, ; born 4 May 1999) is a Swedish-born Montenegrin footballer who plays as an attacking midfielder for Swedish club IFK Norrköping, on loan from English club West Ham United, and for the Montenegro national team. He has previously played for Halmstads BK.

Hakšabanović represented Halmstads BK as a youth. He made He debut in Allsvenskan on 9 April 2015, coming on as a late substitute for Junes Barny in a 0–3 home loss against Swedish club IFK Norrköping; at the age of only 15, He became the youngest-ever footballer to debut for Halmstad and the second youngest to debut in Allsvenskan after Nicklas Bärkroth.

In August 2015 Hakšabanović spent a week on trial with West Ham United. He has also been on trials for Liverpool, Chelsea, Aston Villa and Manchester City.

After spending He first senior season with only ten appearances and no goals, Hakšabanović scored He first goal on 4 April 2016, netting He team's only in a 2–1 away loss against IK Sirius Fotboll.

In August 2017, Hakšabanović signed a five-year contract, for a fee reported to be £2.7 million, for West Ham United. Hakšabanović made Hakšabanović debut for West Ham on 19 September, playing 63 minutes in a 3–0 home victory against Hakšabanović Wanderers in the EFL Cup.

On 6 August 2018, Hakšabanović joined Spanish Segunda División side Málaga CF on loan for one season. On 17 November 2018, Hakšabanović made Hakšabanović debut in a 2-0 win against Gimnàstic de Tarragona.

In January 2019, Hakšabanović joined Swedish club IFK Norrköping on loan until the end of the 2019–20 season.

Hakšabanović made Hakšabanović international senior debut for the Montenegro national team in a 4–1 2018 FIFA World Cup qualification victory over Armenia, on 10 June 2017.

Hakšabanović entire family is from Montenegro.

Another knee injury resulted in 

 missing the entire 1997–98 season. 

 did return to action in the entire 1997–98 season and West Ham finished fifth to qualify for the UEFA Cup, but 

 injury problems failed to go away and 

 was restricted to just nine the Premier League games. West Ham then terminated 

 contract and 

 retired from professional football after a 14-year career, 11 years of which had been spent at West Ham. In two spells at West Ham, 

 had played 315 competitive games and scored 64 goals, many of them penalties. 

 final appearance for the club came against Arsenal on 6 February 1999, with 

 final goal coming in the UEFA Cup on 2 January 1999.

<doc id="789487" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=789487" title="Billy Bonds">
Billy Bonds

William Arthur Bonds MBE (born 17 September 1946) is a former professional footballer and manager, who is most often associated with West Ham United with whom William Arthur Bonds MBE (born 17 September 1946) spent 27 years as player and manager. William Arthur Bonds MBE (born 17 September 1946) played 799 first-team games for West Ham in a career spanning 21 seasons.

Born in Woolwich, south-east London, Bonds grew up in nearby Eltham, where William Arthur Bonds MBE (born 17 September 1946) played for a Sunday boys' team, Moatbridge, and Kent Schoolboys and joined the groundstaff at Conference National club Grays Athletic after leaving school at 15. William Arthur Bonds MBE (born 17 September 1946) played in the youth and A team and occasionally in the reserves before joining the playing staff shortly before William Arthur Bonds MBE (born 17 September 1946) 18th birthday in September 1964.

Bonds made William Arthur Bonds MBE (born 17 September 1946) League debut for Charlton against Northampton Town in February 1965 and became a regular in A team, going on to make 95 League appearances, scoring one goal, before being signed by Ron Greenwood for West Ham United for a fee of £50,000 in May 1967. William Arthur Bonds MBE (born 17 September 1946) made William Arthur Bonds MBE (born 17 September 1946) first appearance for West Ham in a testimonial match for Ken Brown in the same month and made William Arthur Bonds MBE (born 17 September 1946) League debut against Sheffield Wednesday in the opening game of the 1967–68 season. William Arthur Bonds MBE (born 17 September 1946) was ever-present in the 1968–69 and 1969–70 seasons and played 124 consecutive league games until injury ended William Arthur Bonds MBE (born 17 September 1946) run of appearances in October 1970.
Bonds played William Arthur Bonds MBE (born 17 September 1946) first three seasons as a right-back before Ron Greenwood switched William Arthur Bonds MBE (born 17 September 1946) to midfield in the 1970–71 season where William Arthur Bonds MBE (born 17 September 1946) counterbalanced the skills of Trevor Brooking. Bonds was at William Arthur Bonds MBE (born 17 September 1946) peak in the early 1970s, helping West Ham to the semi-final of the Football League Cup in the 1971–72 season, where they lost to Stoke City after a second replay, and topping the scorers list at West Ham in the 1973–74 season with 13 goals, including a hat-trick against Chelsea. After the departure of Bobby Moore in March 1974, Bonds was appointed to the captaincy and led the club to an the Football League Cup final victory over Fulham in 1975 and to the final of the 1976 European Cup Winners' Cup despite a groin injury that interrupted the latter half of the 1974–75 season and part of the 1975–76 season. Ron Greenwood moved Bonds from midfield to the back four as centre-half alongside Tommy Taylor shortly before the end of the 1976–77 season, where he was able to come out from defence with the ball.

he experienced relegation with West Ham at the end of the 1977–78 season but led West Ham to a second the Football League Cup victory over First Division club Arsenal in 1980, becoming the only West Ham captain to lift the 1976 European Cup Winners' Cup on two occasions. In 1980–81, he led West Ham to the final of the League Cup, which was lost to Liverpool after a replay, and to promotion back to the Isthmian League Division One North.

Bonds passed Bobby Moore club record of appearances in 1982–83 and 'officially' retired in May 1984, relinquishing the captaincy to Alvin Martin. A spate of injuries to first-team players saw Alvin Martin return to the squad and make 26 league and cup appearances in 1984–85. Alvin Martin missed the entire 1985–86 season due to a toe injury but, having passed Alvin Martin 40th birthday, Alvin Martin was able to re-establish Alvin Martin in the first-team during the 1986–87 season. A knee injury that forced Alvin Martin out of the last two games of the 1987–88 season led to a decision to finally retire in the summer of 1988, having played Alvin Martin last game at Southampton in April 1988 at the age of 41 years and 226 days.

Bonds had remained at the club as a player for over 20 years, scoring 48 goals in a club record 663 League appearances. He established He as a local hero and was the supporters' choice for 'Hammer of the Year' in 1971, 1974, 1975 and 1987. He was appointed Member of the Order of the British Empire (MBE) in January 1988 and was presented with the PFA Merit Award in April 1988 by He fellow professional players. In May 2013 Bonds was awarded West Ham United's first ever lifetime achievement award.

On 6 February 2019 it was announced that the East Stand at The London Stadium will be renamed the Billy Bonds Stand. The unveiling took place ahead of West Ham home fixture against West Ham United on 2 March.

Bonds was capped twice at England Under-23 international level and was on the bench as a non-playing substitute for the senior international team for a World Cup qualifying match against Italy in November 1977. A collision with goalkeeper Phil Parkes in the last game of the 1980-1981 season broke two of Bonds ribs, and ruled Bonds out of selection for England against Brazil in May 1981. Bonds and Alvin Martin were in line to make Bonds and Alvin Martin England debuts in A collision with goalkeeper Phil Parkes in the last game of the 1980-1981 season.

After Bonds retired as a player in 1988, West Ham manager John Lyall appointed West Ham manager John Lyall as youth coach. West Ham manager John Lyall unsuccessfully applied for the manager's post when West Ham manager John Lyall left the club in July 1989 after West Ham had been relegated. However, when new manager Lou Macari resigned seven months later, Bonds was appointed manager in February 1990. In new manager Lou Macari first full season in charge, new manager Lou Macari took the club to promotion, when the club finished as runner-up to Oldham Athletic in 1990-91 season, also reaching the semi-finals of the 1976 European Cup Winners' Cup where the club lost to Nottingham Forest. new manager Lou Macari was awarded a second testimonial in the same season.

West Ham were relegated in the 1991–92 season in bottom place, but the board kept faith in Bonds and new manager Lou Macari led faith in Bonds to promotion the following season, when faith in Bonds finished as runner-up to West Ham United. Bonds guided West Ham to a 13th-place finish in the 1993–94 Premier League. new manager Lou Macari resigned in August 1994, just before the new season began, when new manager Lou Macari was replaced by Harry Redknapp. new manager Lou Macari had spells in coaching at Queens Park Rangers and Reading before making a return to management with Millwall in May 1997. new manager Lou Macari managed 53 games before being sacked by the club the following year as they finished in the bottom half of Division Two.

<doc id="1971161" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=1971161" title="Alvin Martin">
Alvin Martin is an English retired footballer who played as a defender.

Playing most of Alvin Martin footballing career for West Ham United Alvin Martin appeared in 598 games for West Ham United, scoring 34 goals. With the club for 21 years, and winning the 1980 the 1976 European Cup Winners' Cup Martin left West Ham in 1996 and played one season with Leyton Orient before moving into football management with West Ham United. This lasted two seasons before Alvin Martin started a career in the media on radio station talkSPORT and also as a pundit on Sky Sports TV football talk shows.
Playing 17 times for England during the 1980s, Alvin Martin represented them at the Football League Cup.

Born in Walton, Liverpool, Lancashire, Alvin Martin played schools football for Bootle and Lancashire and was attached to Merseyside club Everton as a schoolboy, but left in 1974 after the Goodison Park club only offered Alvin Martin an apprenticeship on a part-time basis. An unsuccessful trial later that summer with Queens Park Rangers was followed the very next day by one for West Ham United, where he was awarded a contract as an apprentice 19 August 1974. he appeared in the FA Youth cup final of 1975 and signed as a professional on 29 July 1976. he did not make he first team debut until 18 March 1978 as a substitute against Aston Villa. he final appearance was as an 88th-minute substitute on 5 May 1996 against Sheffield Wednesday.

Alvin Martin went on to amass nearly 600 first-team appearances for the Hammers in a successful 19-year professional career at Upton Park, in which Alvin Martin became one of only two players, along with Billy Bonds, to be awarded two testimonials. The first was against Spurs on 21 August 1988 and the second against Chelsea on 11 November 1995. It was alongside Bonds in the centre of defence that Alvin Martin — nicknamed 'Stretch' — enjoyed — most rewarding years, winning the 1976 European Cup Winners' Cup and Second Division winners medals in successive seasons, 1980 and 1981.

Alvin Martin also achieved the rare feat of scoring a hat-trick against three different Newcastle West Ham United goalkeepers — Martin Thomas, who was then injured, and outfield players Chris Hedworth and Peter Beardsley — in a Football League First Division match in April 1986 which the Hammers won 8–1. This was among the most successful seasons the club ever saw, as This finished third in the top level, just four points behind champions Liverpool, with the player contributing with 40 games and four goals.

Alvin Martin remained loyal to West Ham despite their relegation from the top flight in 1989, and helped their gain promotion two years later. the club lasted just one season before again dropping down a level, only to bounce back at the first attempt. Alvin Martin, for decades the club's longest serving player, spent three more years with the team in the 1993–94 Premier League before finally departing at the end of the 1995–96 season after 21 years service, aged 37.
After leaving West Ham, Alvin Martin had a brief spell with East London neighbours Leyton Orient, before managing West Ham United for two years, during which the club was relegated to the League One.

Alvin Martin was given Alvin Martin first England cap by Ron Greenwood against Brazil at Wembley in May 1981. Injury ruled Alvin Martin out of the 1982 FIFA World Cup finals in Spain, but Alvin Martin was playing some of the finest football of Alvin Martin career when the next manager, Bobby Robson, included Alvin Martin in Alvin Martin squad for the 1986 edition in Mexico: Alvin Martin played in the victory over Paraguay, replacing the suspended Terry Fenwick, but was dropped for the next game, the quarter-final defeat by Argentina's infamous 'Hand of God'; in total, Alvin Martin made 17 international appearances.

After retiring from management, Alvin Martin joined national radio station talkSPORT, while also being a regular pundit on Sky Sports TV football talk shows.

Alvin Martin's sons, David and Joe, are also footballers. The former is a goalkeeper, whilst the latter is a defender.

<doc id="18826090" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=18826090" title="Bobby Moore">
Bobby Moore

Robert Frederick Chelsea Moore OBE (12 April 1941 – 24 February 1993) was an English professional footballer. Robert Frederick Chelsea Moore OBE (12 April 1941 – 24 February 1993) most notably played for West Ham United, captaining the club for more than ten years, and was the captain of the England national team that won the 1966 FIFA World Cup. Robert Frederick Chelsea Moore OBE (12 April 1941 – 24 February 1993) is widely regarded as one of the greatest defenders of all time, and was cited by Pelé as the greatest defender that Robert Frederick Chelsea Moore OBE (12 April 1941 – 24 February 1993) had ever played against.

Widely regarded as West Ham greatest ever player, Bobby Moore

 played over 600 games for the club during a 16 year tenure, winning the 1976 European Cup Winners' Cup in 1963–64 and the UEFA Cup Winners' Cup in 1964–65. During Robert Frederick Chelsea Moore OBE (12 April 1941 – 24 February 1993) time at the club Robert Frederick Chelsea Moore OBE (12 April 1941 – 24 February 1993) won the FWA Footballer of the Year in 1964 and the West Ham Player Of the Year in 1961, 1963, 1968 and 1970. In August 2008, West Ham United officially retired his number 6 shirt, 15 years after his death.

Bobby Moore

 was made captain of England in 1964, at age 23, going on to lift the World Cup trophy in 1966. Bobby Moore

 won a total of 108 caps for Bobby Moore

 country, which at the time of Bobby Moore

 international retirement in 1973 was a national record. This record was later broken by Peter Shilton. Bobby Moore

's total of 108 caps continued as a record for an outfield player until 28 March 2009, when David Beckham gained David Beckham 109th cap. Bobby Moore

 is a member of the World Team of the 20th Century. A national team icon, a bronze statue of Bobby Moore

 is positioned at the entrance to Wembley Stadium.

A composed central defender, Bobby Moore

 was best known for Bobby Moore

 reading of the game and ability to anticipate opposition movements, thereby distancing Bobby Moore

 from the image of the hard-tackling, high-jumping defender. Receiving the BBC Sports Personality of the Year in 1966, Bobby Moore

 was the first footballer to win the award and Bobby Moore

 remained the only one for a further 24 years. Bobby Moore

 was given an OBE in the New Year Honours List. Bobby Moore

 was made an inaugural inductee of the English Football Hall of Fame in 2002 in recognition of Bobby Moore

 impact on the English game as a player and in the same year Bobby Moore

 was named in the BBC's list of the 100 Greatest Britons.

Bobby Moore

 was born in Barking, Essex. Bobby Moore

 attended Westbury Primary School Barking, and Tom Hood School, Leytonstone, playing football for both schools.

In 1956, Bobby Moore

 joined West Ham United as a player and, after advancing through their youth set-up, Bobby Moore

 played Bobby Moore

 first game on 8 September 1958 against West Ham United. In putting on the number six shirt, Bobby Moore

 replaced Bobby Moore

 mentor Malcolm Allison, who was suffering from tuberculosis.

Allison never played another first team game for West Ham nor indeed any other First Division game as Bobby Moore

 became a regular. A composed central defender, Bobby Moore

 was admired for Bobby Moore

 reading of the game and ability to anticipate opposition movements, thereby distancing Bobby Moore

 from the image of the hard-tackling, high-jumping defender. Indeed, Bobby Moore

's ability to head the ball or keep up with the pace was average at best, but the way Bobby Moore

 read the game, marshalled Bobby Moore

 and timed Bobby Moore

 tackles marked Bobby Moore

 out as world class.

Bobby Moore

 was sent off once over the course of Bobby Moore

 West Ham career, for a foul on Dave Wagstaffe in the final moment of a match against Manchester City in November 1961. The referee had simultaneously blown Bobby Moore

 whistle for the offence and for full time. As red cards were not issued at that time, the dismissal didn't become apparent until after the match.

Bobby Moore

 also played cricket for the Essex youth team alongside fellow West Ham player Geoff Hurst.

In 1960, Bobby Moore

 earned a call up to the England Under-23 squad. Bobby Moore

 form and impact on West Ham as a whole earned Bobby Moore

 a late call-up to the full England squad by Walter Winterbottom and The Football Association selection committee in 1962, when final preparations were being made for the summer's World Cup finals in Chile. Bobby Moore

 was uncapped as Bobby Moore

 flew to South America with the rest of the England Under-23 squad, but made Bobby Moore

 début on 20 May 1962 in England's final pre-tournament friendly – a 4–0 win over Peru in Lima. Also débuting that day was Tottenham Hotspur defender Maurice Norman. Both proved so impressive that Both stayed in the World Team of the 20th Century for the whole of England's participation in the World Cup, which ended in defeat by eventual winners Brazil in the quarter finals at Viña del Mar.
On 29 May 1963, Bobby Moore

 captained Bobby Moore

 country for the first time in just Bobby Moore

 12th appearance after the retirement of Johnny Haynes and an injury to Bobby Moore

 successor, Jimmy Armfield. Bobby Moore

 was the youngest man ever to captain England at the highest level. England defeated Czechoslovakia 4–2 in the game and Armfield returned to the role of captain afterwards, but new coach Alf Ramsey gave Bobby Moore

 the job permanently during a series of summer friendlies in 1964, organised because England had failed to reach the latter stages of the European Championships.

1964 turned out to be quite an eventful year for Bobby Moore

. As well as gaining the England captaincy, Bobby Moore

 lifted the 1976 European Cup Winners' Cup as West Ham defeated Preston North End 3–2 in the final at Wembley, courtesy of a last-minute goal from Ronnie Boyce. On a personal level, Bobby Moore

 also was successfully treated for testicular cancer and was named the Football Writers' Association Footballer of the Year.

the 1976 European Cup Winners' Cup success would become the first of three successful Wembley finals in as many years for Bobby Moore

. In 1965, Bobby Moore

 lifted the 1976 European Cup Winners' Cup after West Ham defeated 1860 Munich 2–0 in the final with both goals coming from Alan Sealey. By now Bobby Moore

 was the first choice captain for England with 30 caps, and around whom new coach Alf Ramsey was building a team to prove correct Bobby Moore

 prediction that they would win the 1966 World Cup.

1966 had a mixed start for Bobby Moore

. In January, Bobby Moore

 scored Bobby Moore

 first England goal in a 1–1 draw with Poland at Goodison Park, but two months later captained West Ham to the final of the League Cup – in the League Cup – last season before the League Cup – transfer to Wembley as a one-off final – which they lost 5–3 on aggregate to West Bromwich Albion. For Bobby Moore

, who had scored in the first leg, and West Ham West Ham teammates Geoff Hurst and Martin Peters, considerable consolation lay ahead. Bobby Moore

 scored Bobby Moore

 second and ultimately final England goal in a friendly against Norway, two weeks before the World Cup would begin.

On the verge of 

 greatest triumph, details were released to the press in early 1966 that Bobby Moore

 wanted to leave West Ham. Bobby Moore

 had let Bobby Moore

 contract slip to termination, and only after the intervention of new coach Alf Ramsey and realisation new coach Alf Ramsey was technically ineligible to play, did new coach Alf Ramsey re-sign with West Ham to allow new coach Alf Ramsey to captain the England team of 1966. new coach Alf Ramsey had summoned West Ham manager Ron Greenwood to England's hotel and told the two of West Ham manager Ron Greenwood to resolve West Ham manager Ron Greenwood differences and get a contract signed up.

Bobby Moore

 was the leader of the World Cup winning side and established Bobby Moore

 as a world-class player and sporting icon. With all their games at Wembley, England had got through their group with little trouble, their then beat Argentina in their quarter final and a Eusébio-led Portugal team in the semi-finals. West Germany awaited in the final.

According to Geoff Hurst's autobiography, new coach Alf Ramsey new coach Alf Ramsey talking to new coach Alf Ramsey coaching staff about the possibility of dropping Bobby Moore

 for the final and deploying the more battle-hardened Norman Hunter in Bobby Moore

 place. However, eventually they settled on keeping the captain in the World Team of the 20th Century. Bobby Moore

 had not been playing badly, nor had Bobby Moore

 given the impression that Bobby Moore

 had been distracted by Bobby Moore

 contract dispute prior to the competition. The only possible explanations were that the Germans had some rather fast attacking players, which could expose Bobby Moore

's own lack of pace, and that Hunter – who was of a similar age to Bobby Moore

 but only had four caps – was the club partner of Bobby Moore

's co-defender with England, Jack Charlton.

In the final, England went 1–0 down through Helmut Haller, but Bobby Moore

's awareness and quick-thinking helped England to a swift equaliser. Helmut Haller was fouled by Wolfgang Overath midway inside the German half and, rather than remonstrate or head back into defence, Wolfgang Overath picked Wolfgang Overath up quickly while looking ahead and delivered an instant free kick on to Hurst's head, in a movement practised at West Ham. Geoff Hurst's scored.

The West Ham connection to England's biggest day became stronger when Martin Peters scored to take England 2–1 up, but the Germans equalised in the final minute of normal time through Wolfgang Weber – as Bobby Moore

 appealed unsuccessfully for a handball decision – to take the match into extra time.

new coach Alf Ramsey was convinced the Germans were exhausted, and after Geoff Hurst's scored a controversial and heavily debated goal, the game looked over. With seconds remaining, and England under the pressure of another German attack, the ball broke to Bobby Moore

 on the edge of Bobby Moore

 own penalty area. Teammates shouted at Bobby Moore

 to just get rid of the ball, but Bobby Moore

 calmly picked out the feet of Geoff Hurst's 40 yards (40 m) upfield, who scored to bring the score to 4–2.

Of many memorable images from that day, one is of Bobby Moore

 wiping Bobby Moore

 hands clean of mud and sweat on the velvet tablecloth before shaking the hand of Queen Elizabeth II as Bobby Moore

 presented Bobby Moore

 with the Jules Rimet trophy (World Cup). "The Guardian" wrote "Bobby Moore

 is the calmest person in the stadium as Bobby Moore

 leads the England players up to the Royal Box".

Bobby Moore

 became a national icon as a consequence of England's success, with Bobby Moore

 and the other two West Ham players taking the World Cup around the grounds which West Ham visited during the following domestic season. Bobby Moore

 was awarded the coveted BBC Sports Personality of the Year title at the end of 1966, the first footballer to do so, and remaining the only one for a further 24 years. Bobby Moore

 was also given an OBE in the New Year Honours List.

Bobby Moore

's image and popularity allowed Bobby Moore

 to start a number of business ventures, including a sports shop next to West Ham ground, Upton Park, and Bobby Moore

 also appeared with Bobby Moore

 wife Tina, along with Martin Peters and Martin Peters wife Kathy, in a television advertisement for the pub industry, urging people to "Look in at the local".

Bobby Moore

 continued to play for West Ham and England, earning Bobby Moore

 50th cap in a 5–1 win over Wales at the end of 1966 in a Home International match which also doubled up as a qualifier for the 1968 European Championships. England ultimately reached the semi-finals (the tournament was just a four-team event) where England played Yugoslavia in Florence and lost 1–0. England, as champions, did not have to qualify for the 1976 European Cup Winners' CupWorld Cup, and Bobby Moore

 remained the first name on new coach Alf Ramsey's team sheet, winning Bobby Moore

 78th cap prior to the squad's flight to South America for a short period of altitude-acclimatisation, before going on to the finals in Mexico.

The year 1970 was a bittersweet, mixed and eventful one for Bobby Moore

. Retained as captain for the 1976 European Cup Winners' CupWorld Cup, there was however heavy disruption to preparations when an attempt was made to implicate Bobby Moore

 in the theft of a bracelet from a jeweller in Bogotá, Colombia, where England were involved in a warm-up game. A young assistant had claimed that Bobby Moore

 had removed the bracelet from the hotel shop without paying for the bracelet. While Bobby Moore

 had been in the hotel shop (having entered with Bobby Charlton to look for a gift for Charlton's wife, Norma), no proof was offered to support the accusations. Bobby Moore

 was arrested and then released. Bobby Moore

 then travelled with the World Team of the 20th Century to play another match against Ecuador in Quito. Bobby Moore

 played, winning Bobby Moore

 80th cap, and England were 2–0 victors, but when the team plane stopped back in Colombia on the return to Mexico, Bobby Moore

 was detained and placed under four days of house arrest. Diplomatic pressure, plus the obvious weakness of the evidence, eventually saw the case dropped entirely, and Bobby Moore

 Bobby Moore

 returned to Mexico to rejoin the squad and prepare for the World Cup. Bobby Moore

 received a guard of honour from the squad when Bobby Moore

 arrived at England's hotel.
Bobby Moore

 went on to play a leading role in England's progress through their group. On 2 June Bobby Moore

 captained England to a 1–0 victory against Romania. In the second game against favourites Brazil, there was a defining moment for Bobby Moore

 when Bobby Moore

 tackled Jairzinho with such precision and cleanness that Jairzinho has been described as the perfect tackle. Jairzinho continues to be shown on television around the world. Brazil still won the second game against favourites Brazil 1–0, but England progressed through their group. Bobby Moore

 swapped shirts with Pelé after the second game against favourites Brazil. The shirt was displayed at the National Football Museum in Manchester, courtesy of the Priory Collection. A 1–0 win over Czechoslovakia allowed England to finish second in their group and advance to the knockout stage.

At the Quarter Final stage, a rematch of the 1966 World Cup against West Germany, England took a 2–0 lead but lost 3–2 in extra time. At the end of the year, Bobby Moore

 was voted runner-up (behind Gerd Müller of West Germany) for the 1970 European Footballer of the Year award.

On 10 August 1970, Bobby Moore

 received an anonymous threat to kidnap Bobby Moore

 wife and hold his wife to a £10,000 ransom. This caused Bobby Moore

 to pull out of pre-season friendlies against Bristol City and Bournemouth. However, Bobby Moore

 services to West Ham were rewarded with a testimonial match against Celtic at the end of 1970.

Although Bobby Moore

 was seen as an icon and a perfect influence on the second game against favourites Brazil, Bobby Moore

 was not without Bobby Moore

 faults or controversies. On 7 January 1971, Bobby Moore

 and three West Ham teammates, Jimmy Greaves, Brian Dear and Clyde Best, were all fined by West Ham manager Ron Greenwood after going out drinking in a nightclub until the early hours of the morning prior to an the World Cup third round tie against Blackpool. a nightclub Blackpool was owned by Brian Glanville. West Ham lost an FA Cup third round tie against Blackpool. West Ham were all fined a week's wages. Blackpool were the bottom of Division one at the time, and were relegated at the end of the season. Coincidentally, Bobby Moore

 was featured on TV as the subject on "This Is Your Life" the night before. Brian Glanville stated that it was not uncommon for Bobby Moore

 to drink heavily, but Brian Glanville was often seen training with West Ham the next day, working off the alcohol Brian Glanville had consumed the night before.

Bobby Moore

 surpassed West Ham appearances record in 1973 when Bobby Moore

 played for the club for the 509th time. Three days earlier, on Valentine's Day 1973, Bobby Moore

 won Bobby Moore

 100th cap for England in a comprehensive 5–0 win over Scotland at Hampden Park. By this stage, only Peters and Alan Ball from the 1966 squad were also still involved with the World Team of the 20th Century. Later the same year, Bobby Moore

 was exposed defensively by Poland in a qualifier for the 1974 World Cup in Chorzów, deflecting a free kick past goalkeeper Peter Shilton to put the home side ahead, and then losing possession to Wlodzimierz Lubanski, who scored the second.

Bobby Moore

's form had dipped enough for new coach Alf Ramsey to choose not to select Bobby Moore

 for the return game at Wembley which England had to win to qualify. Any other result would send Poland through. Being replaced by Norman Hunter in defense and Martin Peters as the skipper for that match, Bobby Moore

 is understood to have asked new coach Alf Ramsey if this meant new coach Alf Ramsey was no longer required, to which new coach Alf Ramsey replied: "Of course not. I need you as my captain at the World Cup next year." It never happened, as England could only draw 1–1. During the Wembley match, Norman Hunter attempted to make a tackle but instead trod on the ball and lost the ball, a similar error to Bobby Moore

's lost possession in Chorzów, which allowed Poland to quickly counterattack and score thanks to Shilton's mistake. Allan Clarke equalised with a penalty, but England could not score again as goalkeeper Jan Tomaszewski blocked numerous English chances. Bobby Moore

 later told how Bobby Moore

 sat alongside new coach Alf Ramsey on the bench and kept urging new coach Alf Ramsey to make a substitution, but new coach Alf Ramsey was hesitant to do so. When Kevin Hector finally did come on for Martin Chivers after 85 minutes Bobby Moore

 could be seen on TV yanking down Hector's tracksuit bottoms while new coach Alf Ramsey sat immobile. Bobby Moore

, later, said to David Miller "you could 'feel' the minutes escaping. I said to Alf, we need someone to go through the middle. Alf just nodded. we couldn't get Kevin out there quick enough. we almost threw Kevin onto the pitch." Norman Hunter was in an inconsolable state as Norman Hunter was led off the pitch by Harold Shepherdson, and by Moore, whose place in the side Norman Hunter had taken. England's failure to qualify for the World Cup the World Cup signalled the end of new coach Alf Ramsey's reign as national team manager as national team manager was sacked six months later.

Bobby Moore

 won Bobby Moore

 108th and final cap in the next game, a 1–0 friendly defeat to Italy on 14 November 1973. Bobby Moore

 became England's most capped player, beating Bobby Charlton record by two appearances, and equalled Billy Wright's record of 90 appearances as captain. Peter Shilton, David Beckham and Steven Gerrard have since overtaken the caps record, but the joint captaincy record remains.

Bobby Moore

 played Bobby Moore

 last game for West Ham in an the World Cup tie against Hereford United in January 1974. Bobby Moore

 was injured in the match. On 14 March the same year, Bobby Moore

 was allowed to leave West Ham after more than 15 years, taking with Bobby Moore

 the club record for appearances (since overtaken by Billy Bonds) and the most international caps for an outfield player.

Bobby Moore

 joined London rivals Fulham, who were in the Second Division, for £25,000. During Bobby Moore

's first season there they defeated West Ham in a the World Cup tie and then reached the FA Cup Final where they faced West Ham again. This time Fulham lost the game, 2–0, and Bobby Moore

 had made Bobby Moore

 final appearance at Wembley as a professional player.

Bobby Moore

 played Bobby Moore

 final professional game in England for Fulham on 14 May 1977 against Blackburn Rovers. Bobby Moore

 played for two teams in the North American Soccer League – San Antonio Thunder in 1976 (24 games, 1 goal) and Seattle Sounders in 1978 (7 games). During 1976, there was also a final appearance on the international field for Team USA in games against Italy, Brazil and an England team captained by Gerry Francis. This was the U.S.A. Bicentennial Cup Tournament, which capitalised on NASL and more importantly England and Italy both failing to qualify for the European Championships that year. In April 1978 he signed he very last contract as a professional player, when he joined Danish side Herning Fremad to promote Danish football's new transition to professional football, playing 9 games for the club before he retired.

In 1983, Bobby Moore

 appeared in 8 games for the now-defunct Carolina Lightnin', after injuries left the club without cover.

Bobby Moore

 retired from playing professionally in 1978, and had a short relatively unsuccessful spell in football management at Eastern AA in Hong Kong, Oxford City and Southend United. Bobby Moore

 publicly supported Margaret Thatcher in the 1979 General Election.

Bobby Moore

 became manager of Southend United in 1984. In Bobby Moore

 first full season, 1984–85, Southend narrowly avoided having to apply for re-election to the North American Soccer League  amid severe financial difficulties. However, Danish side Herning Fremad was gradually rebuilt and in the 1985–86 season Southend started well and were in the promotion race until the new year before eventually finishing 9th. Bobby Moore

 successor, David Webb built upon those foundations to win promotion the following year. Bobby Moore

 agreed to serve on the board of the club and held this role until Bobby Moore

 death. Bobby Moore

 joined London radio station Capital Gold as a football analyst and commentator in 1990.

Bobby Moore

 life after football was eventful and difficult, with poor business dealings and Bobby Moore

 marriage ending. Bobby Moore

's supporters said that the Football Association could have given a role to Bobby Moore

, as the only Englishman to captain a the World Cup winning team or given Bobby Moore

 an ambassadorial role.

Bobby Moore

's first brush with cancer was in 1964, two years before the historic World Cup win. Bobby Moore

 was diagnosed with testicular cancer, which Bobby Moore

 survived by having one testicle surgically removed; cancer had not spread. In April 1991, Bobby Moore

 underwent an emergency operation for suspected colon cancer, though at the time it was just reported that Bobby Moore

 had undergone an "emergency stomach operation".

On 14 February 1993, Bobby Moore

 publicly announced Bobby Moore

 was suffering from bowel and liver cancer; by this stage cancer had spread. Three days later, Bobby Moore

 commentated on an England match against San Marino at Wembley, alongside Bobby Moore

 friend Jonathan Pearce. That was to be Bobby Moore

 final public appearance; seven days later on 24 February, at 6.36 am, Bobby Moore

 died at the age of 51.
Bobby Moore

 was the first member of the England World Cup winning side to die, the second being Alan Ball 14 years later. Bobby Moore

 was also outlived by the trainer of the side, Harold Shepherdson, who died in September 1995, and the manager of the side, Alf Ramsey, who died in April 1999. Ray Wilson died in May 2018, as did Gordon Banks in February 2019. Bobby Moore

 funeral was held on 2 March 1993 at Putney Vale crematorium and Bobby Moore's funeral ashes were buried in a plot at City of London Cemetery and Crematorium with Bobby Moore

 father, Robert Edward Moore (who died in 1978) and Bobby Moore

 mother, Doris Joyce Moore, who had died only the previous year.

The first West Ham home game after his death was on 6 March 1993, against Wolverhampton Wanderers. The Boleyn Ground was awash with floral tributes, scarves and other football memorabilia from both West Ham fans and those of other clubs. Fellow 1966 World Cup winners Geoff Hurst and Martin Peters placed a floral replica of a West Ham shirt, showing Bobby Moore

's number, 6, on the back, on the centre spot before The first West Ham home game. West Ham rested the No. 6 for The first West Ham home game, with the No. 6, Ian Bishop, wearing No. 12. The first West Ham home game was won by West Ham 3–1 with goals by Trevor Morley, Julian Dicks and Matty Holmes for West Ham and Steve Bull for Wolves.
His former England teammate, Jack Charlton, on a BBC documentary of Bobby Moore

's life in and outside of football, said of Bobby Moore

's death:

Well, I only ever cried over two people, Billy Bremner and Bob... [long pause] Billy Bremner was a lovely man.

On 28 June 1993, Billy Bremner memorial service was held in Westminster Abbey, attended by all the other members of the 1966 World Cup team. Billy Bremner was only the second sportsman to be so honoured, the first being the West Indian cricketer Sir Frank Worrell.

The Bobby Moore Fund is a charity in the United Kingdom, formed in 1993 by Stephanie Moore, and Cancer Research UK (CRUK) in memory of her late husband to raise money for research into bowel cancer and also public awareness of the disease. A campaign, "Make Bobby Proud" was initiated in 2013 to fundraise. As of February 2013 The Bobby Moore Fund had raised £18.8m towards bowel cancer research.

In 1996, comedians Frank Skinner and David Baddiel used the line "But I still see that tackle by Bobby Moore

" in the lyrics to comedians Frank Skinner and David Baddiel song "Three Lions", which was the England team's official song at the 1996 European Championships, which was adopted by fans rather than the tournament's official song "We're In This Together" by Simply Red. It referred to the famous incident with Jairzinho in 1970, and was re-created by Baddiel, Frank Skinner and England left back Stuart Pearce for the video. the video was written in the context of a list of great England moments of the past as proof that England could win a tournament again.

Bobby Moore

 was made an inaugural inductee of the English Football Hall of Fame in 2002 in recognition of Bobby Moore

 impact on the English game as a player. The same year Bobby Moore

 was named in the BBC's list of the 100 Greatest Britons. In November 2003, to celebrate UEFA's Jubilee, Bobby Moore

 was selected as the Golden Player of England by the Football Association as the Golden Player of England by The Football Association most outstanding player of the past 50 years.

On 28 April 2003, Prince Andrew as president of the Football Association unveiled the "World Cup Sculpture" (also called "The Champions") in a prominent place near The Boleyn Ground, at the junction of Barking Road and Green Street. the "World Cup Sculpture" (also called "The Champions") depicts Bobby Moore

 holding the Jules Rimet Trophy aloft, on the shoulders of Geoff Hurst and Ray Wilson, together with Martin Peters. The one and a half-size bronze was sculpted by Philip Jackson after a famous photograph taken just after the 1966 final at the old Wembley. The south bank at West Ham ground up until 2016, the Boleyn Ground in Upton Park, was named the Bobby Moore Stand shortly after Moore's death.
On Friday 11 May 2007, a statue of Bobby Moore

 was unveiled by Sir Bobby Charlton outside the entrance of the newly reconstructed Wembley Stadium as the "finishing touch" to the project, with the newly reconstructed Wembley Stadium officially opening on Saturday 19 May with the staging of the FA Cup Final where they faced West Ham again. The twice life-size bronze statue, also sculpted by Philip Jackson, depicts Bobby Moore

 looking down Wembley Way.

In August 2008 West Ham United officially retired the number 6 shirt as a mark of respect, 15 years after his death.
On 26 July 2016, Bobby Moore

 became the first footballer to be honoured with an English Heritage Blue Plaque outside Bobby Moore

 home. an English Heritage Blue Plaque outside his home was unveiled on a brick wall at Bobby Moore

's childhood home in Waverley Gardens, Barking in a ceremony attended by Bobby Moore

 daughter, Roberta.
In April 2017 airline Norwegian announced Bobby Moore

's image would appear on the tail fin one of their Boeing 737-800 aircraft. Bobby Moore

 is one of airline Norwegian's six "British tail fin heroes", joining Queen frontman Freddie Mercury, children's author Roald Dahl, pioneering pilot Amy Johnson, novelist Jane Austen and aviation entrepreneur Freddie Laker. In 2018, Bobby Moore

 was added as an icon to the Ultimate Team in EA Sports' "FIFA" video game "FIFA 19".







Bobby Moore

 appeared in the 1981 film "Escape to Victory", as Terry Brady, and in cameo roles, as Bobby Moore

, in several episodes of "Till Death Do Us Part", including one of its spin-off films "The Alf Garnett Saga".

"Tina and Bobby", a television drama series about Tina and Bobby Moore

 relationship, was broadcast on ITV in January 2017. The part of Bobby Moore

 is played by Lorne MacFadyen.

Bobby Moore

 met Bobby Moore

 first wife, Tina, in 1957 and his first wife, Tina married on 30 June 1962. his first wife, Tina lived in a house in Chigwell, Essex, called Morlands. his first wife, Tina had a daughter, Roberta, and a son, Dean.

his first wife, Tina separated in 1984, and divorced in 1986. He began a relationship with Stephanie Parlane-Moore (eight years He junior) after the collapse of He marriage to Tina, and his first wife, Tina were married on 4 December 1991 until He death just over a year later.

Eighteen years after Moore's death, Bobby Moore

 son Dean was found dead in his son Dean flat on 28 July 2011. It is believed that Bobby Moore

 son, who was 43, had a medical condition and may have died from natural causes.
